Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which runch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Cribs","url":"\/shows\/tc-cribs","attr":"","target":"","classes":[""],"description":"","object_id":1605180,"object":"custom","type":"custom","type_label":"Custom Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2290158,"date":"2022-03-30T15:45:10","date_gmt":"2022-03-30T22:45:10","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2290158"},"modified":"2022-03-31T09:41:04","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T16:41:04","slug":"ycombinator-open-source-startups-winter-22-demo-day","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/30\/ycombinator-open-source-startups-winter-22-demo-day\/","title":{"rendered":"8 open source companies from YC Demo Day Winter &#8217;22"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Wicked fast VPNs, data organization tools, auto-generated videos to spice up your company\u2019s Instagram stories \u2026 Y Combinator\u2019s Winter 2022 open source founders have some interesting ideas up their sleeves. And since they\u2019re open source, some of these companies will let you join in on the fun of collaboration too. Here are all of the open source related companies presenting at Demo Day in the Winter 2022 cohort.<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/tuvahealth.com\/\">Tuva Health<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2021<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Salt Lake City, Utah<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2290158\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Tuva cleans messy healthcare data to help the healthcare industry build scalable data products.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Tuva wants to become the open standard for healthcare data transformation and build the data network for multisite benchmarking and research.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Tuva uses machine learning to further develop its technology.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Co-founders Coco (Jorge) Zuloaga and Aaron Neiderhiser have worked in healthcare data science for a decade. They\u2019re using that experience to help digital health companies get their data ready for analytics and machine learning.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Have you ever gone to the doctor and waited for minutes while the nurse\u2019s computer \u2014 running Windows 2000 \u2014 struggles to open your chart, only to find that they don\u2019t have updated information about what meds you\u2019re on? We can only imagine how mind-numbingly tedious it would be for health tech companies to organize all this stuff, so it seems like Tuva Health is doing a good service by making their software open source. Now, to get that nurse off of Windows 2000\u2026<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/firez.one\">Firezone<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2021<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Mountain View, California<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Firezone is building an open source alternative to OpenVPN and Cisco AnyConnect using a new VPN protocol called WireGuard. The company is targeting businesses to help remote workers access private networks.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Apparently, using WireGuard makes Firezone faster than its competitors.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Speed! Cryptography! It\u2019s also worth noting that fellow cohort members Netmaker are also developing open source software based on WireGuard.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Co-founder Jamil Bou Kheir spent eight years at Cisco, a direct competitor! Spicy! Bou Kheir also lived in a \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/imgur.com\/a\/ujsmGH7\">tiny hacker house<\/a>\u201d for two years, which \u2026 while we don\u2019t want to know what the tiny hacker house smells like, we appreciate the out-of-the-box idea.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Faster VPN options? Sounds good to us. We\u2019re a bit more fixated on the tiny hacker house, though. What\u2019s going on there?<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/www.growthbook.io\">GrowthBook<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2020<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Palo Alto, California<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> GrowthBook is an open source platform to help companies make data-driven product decisions with feature flags and A\/B tests.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> GrowthBook focuses on feature flagging and experimentation and operates under the ethos that this is the best way to build products at scale.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> GrowthBook says that an existing SaaS solution, LaunchDarkly, requires a company to send them all of their data, which poses high costs and security concerns. GrowthBook says it solves this by using a company\u2019s existing data infrastructure and business metrics.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Co-founders Jeremy Dorn and Graham McNicoll both used to work at <a href=\"http:\/\/Education.com\">Education.com<\/a> as chief architect and CTO respectively. After <a href=\"http:\/\/Education.com\">Education.com<\/a>\u2019s exit in 2019, the two of them began working on GrowthBook.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Startups will likely be more comfortable using open source software to help them make product decisions rather than sending all of their data to a third-party provider.<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/www.eventualcomputing.com\">Eventual<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2022<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> San Francisco, California<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Eventual is a data warehouse for images and video, making it easier for enterprise machine learning teams to design continuous pipelines that ingest, organize and process imaging data.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Eventual wants to help companies save time and money by optimizing workflow.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Eventual says that it\u2019s the first turn-key data warehouse for images and video. Instead of using SQL, Eventual\u2019s query interface is a Lambda function that can be written in the programming language of your choice.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Jay Chia and Sammy Sidhu both have backgrounds in deep learning \u2014 they worked together on <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/26\/lyft-sells-self-driving-unit-to-toyotas-woven-planet-for-550m\/\">Lyft Level 5<\/a> to build autonomous driving technology that was acquired by Toyota.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> If these founders can get cars to drive autonomously, data organization via machine learning should be a piece of cake, right? (At least it\u2019s a business endeavor less likely to result in an accident.)<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/gravitl.com\">Netmaker<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2021<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Asheville, North Carolina<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Netmaker is an open source tool based on the WireGuard VPN protocol.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Netmaker claims to operate 15 times faster than OpenVPN.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Netmaker and its cohort-mate Firezone are both open source, faster alternatives to existing VPN software.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> CTO Dillon Carns and CEO Alex Feiszli left their software engineering gigs to develop Netmaker. Feiszli formerly served as a senior engineer at IBM, a consultant at Deloitte and a contractor for Red Hat.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Without testing the products, we can\u2019t really say whether Netmaker or its cohort-mate Firezone is faster, but we do know that Netmaker\u2019s CTO has a dog named Pepper. The ball\u2019s in your court, Firezone.<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/trytoolchest.com\">Toolchest<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2021<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Mountain View, California<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Per Toolchest\u2019s website, \u201cWe have felt the pain of implementing and scaling computational biology tools. We&#8217;re here to build better core tooling for bioinformatics.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Toolchest says it will make it possible for drug discovery companies to get analysis results up to 100 times faster.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Users don\u2019t need to migrate their data or learn how to use a new platform. Toolchest makes implementing and scaling computational biology tools just three lines of code.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> CTO Bryce Cai has an academic background, researching computational chemistry and mathematics at Stanford. CEO Noah Lebovic previously lead software engineering at a now-acquired microbiome startup.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Toolchest is so open source that its signature three lines of code are literally just on the homepage of their website.<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/www.unai.one\/\">Unai<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2021<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> San Francisco, California<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Unai is developing a VR headset and virtual world that aims to help people feel connected to one another in the virtual world.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Unai wants to make VR interactions look, feel and sound like they do in real life.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Unai believes that \u201cvirtual presence\u201d is the \u201cfirst killer use case\u201d for VR, not gaming.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Maxim Perumal built Relativity, an open source VR headset, at age 15. Now, as CEO of Unai, Perumal recruited a team with former senior engineers from companies like Apple, Nvidia, Intel, Activision, Meta and Sony.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Since Unai is still in stealth, it\u2019s hard to say what makes its technology different from mainstream headsets like the Meta Quest 2. But we cannot understate Unai\u2019s biggest advantage, which is that Mark Zuckerberg is not its CEO.<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/instantdomains.com\/\">Instant Domains<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2022<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Victoria, Canada<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Instant Domains claims that in less time than it takes to create a social media profile, businesses can buy a domain, launch a site and start collecting revenue.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Instant Domains is encrypted and promises to never collect data about its users.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Technically, you can set up a Squarespace or a Wix site pretty fast too \u2014 but Instant Domains says it&#8217;s even faster and easier. It may not be as flexible as other no-code website builders, but it\u2019s less expensive ($10 a year for a domain, plus an optional $5 a month for extra features). Some business owners might not need all of the bells and whistles on other platforms.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Instant Domains is an outgrowth of Instant Domain Search, a side project that CEO Beau Hartshorne built in 2005, which now makes around $1 million in annual revenue. Hartshorne is joined by CTO Dirkjan Ochtman, a 20-year veteran in software engineering and accomplished open source maintainer.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Hot take: Squarespace is expensive. Normally, I urge people to just make a free WordPress site and attach their own domain to it, but if Instant Domains can accomplish what it sets out to, maybe we won\u2019t have to mess around in cPanel to get an affordable website up and running. Instant Domains kind of feels like Linktree but with custom domain management built in.<\/p>\n<h2><a href=\"https:\/\/uberduck.ai\/\">Uberduck<\/a><\/h2>\n<p><strong>Founded:<\/strong> 2021<\/p>\n<p><strong>Location:<\/strong> Seattle, Washington<\/p>\n<p><strong>What it says it does:<\/strong> Uberduck calls itself \u201cCanva for programmable video,\u201d making video that can be automatically generated via API.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Promises include:<\/strong> Within minutes, Uberduck will generate dynamic videos that can be personalized with customer data. Uberduck can also be used to develop advertisements and social media posts. You can also \u2026 clone your voice? Deepfake yourself? Use wisely.<\/p>\n<p><strong>How it says it differs from rivals:<\/strong> Uberduck boasts a Discord community of almost 3,000 members who collaborate to turn AI research into design tools for the app.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Founders:<\/strong> Samson Koelle holds a Ph.D. in statistics and has worked for places like Amazon and the National Institutes of Health. Koelle is joined by co-founders William Luer and Zach Wener, who was once an editorial fellow at The Atlantic (is the tech journalist to tech founder pipeline a thing?).<\/p>\n<p><strong>Our thoughts:<\/strong> Finally, a startup that calls itself \u201cCanva for [use case]\u201d that actually makes sense in comparison to Canva.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/yc-demo-day-winter-2022\/\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/YC-DD-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about YC Demo Day on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Wicked fast VPNs, data organization tools, auto-generated videos to spice up your company\u2019s Instagram stories \u2026 Y Combinator\u2019s Winter 2022 open source founders have some interesting ideas up their sleeves. And since they\u2019re open source, some of these companies will let you join in on the fun of collaboration too. It&#8217;s the same old features that have been around for months, just cooler and more wizard-like. As long as you&#8217;re using two touch-screen Apple devices with the same Apple ID, you should be good to go.<\/p>\n<p>If you knew about this already, congrats. wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=5938293"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":290463,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/touchscreens\/","name":"Touchscreens","slug":"touchscreens","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/290463"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=290463"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=290463"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=290463"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=290463"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2291477,"date":"2022-03-30T09:51:37","date_gmt":"2022-03-30T16:51:37","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2291477"},"modified":"2022-03-30T13:38:56","modified_gmt":"2022-03-30T20:38:56","slug":"tiktok-snapchat-parental-controls-attorneys-general","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/30\/tiktok-snapchat-parental-controls-attorneys-general\/","title":{"rendered":"State attorneys want TikTok and Snap to support third-party parental control apps"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">TikTok and Snapchat need more parental controls, a <a href=\"https:\/\/1li23g1as25g1r8so11ozniw-wpengine.netdna-ssl.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/NAAG-Final-Letter-Parental-Control-App.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">letter<\/a> signed by 44 attorneys general stated.<\/p>\n<p>Yesterday, the National Association of Attorneys General (NAAG) sent a series of <a href=\"https:\/\/www.naag.org\/policy-letter\/naag-urges-tiktok-and-snapchat-to-give-parents-more-control\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">concerns<\/a> to the two social apps, which are commonly used among teens.<\/p>\n<p>The attorneys general cited a range of problems they had with the social media apps, including, more broadly, the negative impact they can have on the physical, emotional and mental well-being of children and teens. They also noted that content depicting abusive sexual relationships can seriously harm a child&#8217;s view of a healthy relationship, helping to perpetuate domestic abuse and human trafficking. And the letter stressed that TikTok and Snapchat don&#8217;t effectively collaborate with third-party parental control apps to allow parents to monitor and restrict what their children can do on their platforms.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2291477\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The NAAG cited a study from one such app, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bark.us\/annual-report-2021\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bark<\/a>, which analyzed 3.4 billion messages in 2021 across 30 apps to find that 74.6% of teens were involved in a self-harm\/suicidal situation, 90.73% encountered nudity or sexual content online and 93.31% engaged in conversations about drugs or alcohol.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cParental control apps can alert parents or schools to messages and posts on your platforms that have the potential to be harmful and dangerous. Apps can also alert parents if their child manifests a desire for self-harm or suicide,\u201d the letter reads.<\/p>\n<p>Snapchat already has some in-app <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/instagram-rolls-out-new-safety-tools-for-parents\/\">parental controls<\/a>, as does <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/17\/tiktok-expands-parental-controls-to-include-search-commenting-and-account-privacy\/\">TikTok<\/a>, but this group of attorneys general wants the platforms to be more compatible with third-party parental control apps, though they didn\u2019t endorse a particular product. They suggested that parental control apps could access social media app features like private messaging, which the built-in parental controls don&#8217;t monitor. Plus, third-party apps could better filter the user-generated content that appears in the apps&#8217; main feeds.<\/p>\n<p>Still, third-party control apps introduce their own swath of problems regarding which tactics they use to surveil children.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Though TikTok and Snapchat did already have parental controls, its competitor Instagram did not. After a series of Senate hearings about the impact of social media on teen mental health, Meta recently began rolling out <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/instagram-rolls-out-new-safety-tools-for-parents\/\">parental controls<\/a> on Instagram, a long-overdue safety measure.<\/p>\n<p>But teen safety on these platforms remains a concern in the U.S. government, regardless of whether or not parental controls are in place. President Biden even mentioned the threat of social media to teen mental health in his <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/biden-social-media-mental-health-state-of-the-union\/\">State of the Union address<\/a>, which former Facebook employee and whistleblower Frances Haugen attended as an honored guest.<\/p>\n<p>TikTok is more popular among teens than Instagram, which has <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/11\/instagram-bonuses-reels-tiktok\/\">poured money<\/a> into its TikTok clone Reels to keep up. But as TikTok holds its ground as the fastest-growing social app, Meta has gone to even more dramatic lengths to maintain its prominence. The Washington Post <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/technology\/2022\/03\/30\/facebook-tiktok-targeted-victory\/?request-id=223d214e-1ead-4b0f-80b5-3586e0ed866c&amp;pml=1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported today<\/a> that Meta hired Targeted Victory, a Republican consulting firm, to turn the public against TikTok. In some cases, Targeted Victory attempted to influence public opinion by claiming that certain dangerous viral trends began on TikTok, though they actually <a href=\"https:\/\/www.insider.com\/slap-a-teacher-challenge-tiktok-october-trend-2021-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">started on Facebook<\/a>. TechCrunch also <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/11\/30\/facebook-targeted-victory-definers-gop\/\">reported<\/a> in 2018 that Facebook had worked with Targeted Victory to help slow progress on legislation that would impact the platform\u2019s political ad spending.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cTargeted Victory\u2019s corporate practice manages bipartisan teams on behalf of our clients. It is public knowledge we have worked with Meta for several years and we are proud of the work we have done,&#8221; the firm&#8217;s CEO Zac Moffatt said in a statement.<\/p>\n<p>In any case, there&#8217;s only so much that parental controls can do to keep apps safe for teens &#8212; it&#8217;s on the apps themselves too to make sure that they aren&#8217;t serving teens unsafe content.<\/p>\n<p><em>Update, 3\/30\/22 at 4:38 PM EST with statement from Targeted Victory.<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"3nLetIxmE5\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/11\/30\/facebook-targeted-victory-definers-gop\/\">Facebook quietly hired Republican strategy firm Targeted Victory<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook quietly hired Republican strategy firm Targeted Victory&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/11\/30\/facebook-targeted-victory-definers-gop\/embed\/#?secret=MtwdorjDEB#?secret=3nLetIxmE5\" data-secret=\"3nLetIxmE5\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AOVwHEQr7K\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/biden-social-media-mental-health-state-of-the-union\/\">Biden will address social media&#8217;s mental health impact at State of the Union<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; controls","slug":"parental-controls","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/973655"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=973655"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=973655"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=973655"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=973655"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":7054,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/senate\/","name":"senate","slug":"senate","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/7054"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=7054"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=7054"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=7054"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=7054"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":80687524,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/snapchat\/","name":"Snapchat","slug":"snapchat","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/80687524"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=80687524"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=80687524"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=80687524"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=80687524"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2290875,"date":"2022-03-29T12:43:54","date_gmt":"2022-03-29T19:43:54","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2290875"},"modified":"2022-03-29T22:01:08","modified_gmt":"2022-03-30T05:01:08","slug":"yc-demo-day-competition","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/yc-demo-day-competition\/","title":{"rendered":"Is YC turning into a kind of fight club?"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Since inception, Y Combinator has invested in thousands of startups, and more recently, even hundreds within a single batch. Given the accelerator\u2019s growth, competitive tensions feel nearly inevitable.<\/p>\n<p>Still, one has to wonder if there is a fundamental shift afoot. Whereas YC always backed companies that might at some point overlap, the outfit appeared to casting its net far and wide, bringing in different startups at different stages from different geographies \u2014 companies that used each other\u2019s products and formed tight bonds through YC\u2019s active alumni network.<\/p>\n<p>Now, however, YC seems to be actively leaning into startups that are roughly the same age, operating in the same countries and targeting exactly the same opportunity with nearly identical business models. Indeed, while similar types of companies within a class had grown inescapable as YC\u2019s class sizes have ballooned, a kind of sameness is more apparent than ever with its latest batch of 400 startups. In fact, it&#8217;s beginning to look like the plan here is to back as many nascent rival teams as possible \u2014 then let them duke it out.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2290875\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Perhaps unsurprisingly, Y Combinator sees things differently. At least, asked about the many startups that would seem to compete from the outset, a spokeswoman for YC writes in an email: &#8220;These companies are not in the same groups and do not interact. Also, it is common for startups to pivot during the batch.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In the meantime, we\u2019ve rounded up some of the startups that seem to<em> us<\/em> to overlap \u2014 a lot \u2014 within its Winter 2022 batch.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<h2><strong>TradeX and Better Opinions<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Founded in the same year and same location, TradeX and Better Opinions have the same goal: give people a way to bet \u2014 and win \u2014 money on their predictions. The startups are building platforms where people can trade money while betting on whether or not an outcome will happen, from a movie launch to who the next president will be. There are more serious future events to bet on as well, such as climate change, inflation and whether omicron cases will rise or fall in a particular location.<\/p>\n<p>The only clear difference between the two companies is that TradeX is targeting higher income Indians and Better Opinions is branding itself more around inclusivity and accessibility.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<h2><strong>Firezone and Netmaker<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>As early as 2018, our own Romain Dillet was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/07\/28\/how-i-made-my-own-wireguard-vpn-server\/\">making his own VPN server<\/a> using WireGuard, a faster and more secure alternative to existing VPN software. Firezone and Netmaker, both participants in this batch of Y Combinator startups, are open source VPNs built atop WireGuard. Netmaker claims it\u2019s 15x faster than OpenVPN, a popular VPN software, while Firezone says it\u2019s 4x faster. But speed isn\u2019t everything \u2014 the competitor cohort-mates will have to battle it out to offer better customer service, firewall options and ease of use than the other. Both startups have a free plan and a paid plan for larger business teams, but neither company is sharing pricing for these paid plans, so we can\u2019t compare their price points just yet.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>Streak and Yodaa<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Consider that Streak and Yodaa are both less than two years old, both based in Bangalore, and both trying to build banking businesses that cater to teenagers by both educating them on their spending and helping them to save. (Both also offer a gamified approach, wherein kids can earn coins for certain spending behaviors.) It\u2019s fairly plain these two will be vying for the same customers, who probably won\u2019t be using two different banking apps. (<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/a-look-at-all-35-international-fintech-startups-at-ycs-winter-2022-demo-day\/\">More here<\/a>.)<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"rpoJ9QCfxi\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/y-combinator-india-winter-2022\/\">India dominates Y Combinator\u2019s latest startup batch (again)<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;India dominates Y Combinator\u2019s latest startup batch (again)&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/y-combinator-india-winter-2022\/embed\/#?secret=wBLAOU5VRM#?secret=rpoJ9QCfxi\" data-secret=\"rpoJ9QCfxi\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<h2><strong>Finku and Pina and Sribuu<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>All <em>three<\/em> of these companies are personal financial adviser startups that are based in Jakarta and have been founded in the last year or two. Yes, Indonesia is a big market, but also, come on.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>Tradezi and Anfin<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Tradezi is a months-old, Ho Chi Minh City, Vietnam-based startup that calls itself the \u201cRobinhood for Southeast Asia.\u201d What it does (or will do): offers free online trading accounts that allows users to invest in stocks, crypto and other alternative assets in one place. It sounds a lot like Anfin, which is a year-old, Ho Chi Minh City-based startup that\u2019s building a digital brokerage in Vietnam connecting users to the stock market in \u201ca simple and intuitive way.\u201d Investors could sign up for both companies\u2019 brokerage accounts, but would they?<\/p>\n<h2><strong>Clupp and Momento<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>The insurance market, particularly for vehicles, is far from saturated in Latin America, with just 30% of cars and 10% of motorcycles covered, according to Clupp, an online insurance startup that was founded in 2021 and is based in Mexico City. Indeed, Clupp sees a big opportunity in providing more affordable insurance for low-risk drivers in Latin America. And so does Momento, which was also founded in 2021 and based in Mexico City and is also looking to insure the region&#8217;s drivers and motorcycle riders. The big difference (for now): Momento says it is working through the regulatory process to be a fully licensed insurance carrier; Clupp appears to be working <em>with<\/em> a fully licensed insurance carrier to offer its products (Mapfre for cars and HDI for motorcycles).<\/p>\n<h2><strong>beU delivery and HeyFood<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Before this year, YC hadn&#8217;t backed a food delivery startup in Africa. So it was a bit surprising to see two of this type of company &#8212; beU delivery and HeyFood &#8212; in a single batch.<\/p>\n<p>We understand that YC is excited to back food delivery businesses after seeing <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/08\/doordash-ipo-pricing\/\">DoorDash go public<\/a>. These startups operate in far apart African markets &#8212; beU delivery in Ethiopia and HeyFood in Nigeria &#8212; but over time, they&#8217;ll expand into similar markets and compete for the same customers in their bids to become the region&#8217;s top delivery platform.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>Dojah and Identity Pass<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Both platforms, founded in 2021 and based in Lagos, play in the identity verification space. Dojah claims to be an &#8220;all-in-one know-your-customer (KYC) and identity verification platform for Africa,&#8221; while Identity Pass says its infrastructure makes it possible for digital businesses in Africa to \u201ceasily verify their customers within seconds.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s easy to assume that the market is enormous for both players, but customers will have to choose one of two services or switch periodically depending on speed, level of insights they offer, who fights fraud better and price points.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p>Naturally, even startups with a different take may be jockeying for the space soon enough. As we have seen with fintech especially, all financial technology products <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/fintech-tam-explained-by-dating-apps\/\">go horizontal until they blur<\/a>. This is why SoFi now features stock investing, Robinhood offers a debit card and so forth. Once you go through the work of bringing a consumer into the fold, you want them to sell them as many products as possible &#8212; so you keep adding.<\/p>\n<p>That means that regardless of where this cohort is starting (some are robo advisers, some Robinhood clones, some neobanks, some insurtech, <em>many<\/em> are tackling carbon emissions), Y Combinator has invested money and energy into numerous companies that could find themselves competing with one another sooner rather than later. While they may form friendships and become one another&#8217;s customers, you can also easily foresee, in some markets, more battle royale than mere dustup.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/yc-demo-day-winter-2022\/\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/YC-DD-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about YC Demo Day on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Since inception, Y Combinator has invested in thousands of startups, and more recently, even hundreds within a single batch. Given the accelerator\u2019s growth, competitive tensions feel nearly inevitable. Still, one has to wonder if there is a fundamental shift afoot. Whereas YC always backed companies that might at some point overlap, the outfit appeared to 2022","slug":"yc-demo-day-winter-2022","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576998959"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576998959"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576998959"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576998959"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576998959"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2290260,"date":"2022-03-28T14:38:40","date_gmt":"2022-03-28T21:38:40","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2290260"},"modified":"2022-03-29T06:32:28","modified_gmt":"2022-03-29T13:32:28","slug":"spotify-covid-19-content-advisory-joe-rogan","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/28\/spotify-covid-19-content-advisory-joe-rogan\/","title":{"rendered":"Spotify&#8217;s COVID-19 content advisory continues roll out two months after Joe Rogan uproar"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">You probably remember a few months ago when you couldn&#8217;t turn on the news, check Twitter or talk to your conservative uncle without broaching the issue of Joe Rogan, who is signed to an exclusive deal with Spotify worth <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2022\/02\/17\/arts\/music\/spotify-joe-rogan-misinformation.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">more than $200 million<\/a>. In January,\u00a0270 physicians and scientists published an <a href=\"https:\/\/www.rollingstone.com\/culture\/culture-news\/covid-misinformation-joe-rogan-spotify-petition-1282240\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">open letter<\/a> to Spotify demanding that it institute misinformation policies in light of Rogan&#8217;s podcast, which <a href=\"https:\/\/podcastcharts.byspotify.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tops\u00a0Spotify&#8217;s charts<\/a> and has <a href=\"https:\/\/www.mediamatters.org\/joe-rogan-experience\/joe-rogan-wrapped-year-covid-19-misinformation-right-wing-myths-and-anti-trans\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">repeatedly served as a platform<\/a> for false narratives about the virus. Then, musical icons like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/26\/spotify-neil-young-joe-rogan\/\">Neil Young<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/29\/joni-mitchell-joins-neil-young-pulls-her-music-from-spotify-over-vaccine-misinformation\/\">Joni Mitchell<\/a> pulled their libraries from the platform in protest, prompting Spotify to belatedly publish its <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.spotify.com\/2022-01-30\/spotify-platform-rules\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">platform rules<\/a>. Now, Spotify finally rolled out a content advisory warning on podcasts that discuss COVID-19, two months after it committed to launching the feature.<\/p>\n<p>The advisory is a blue bar that appears atop episodes of podcasts that discuss COVID-19, prompting listeners to click to learn more. This directs users to its <a href=\"https:\/\/open.spotify.com\/genre\/corona_news_podcasts-page\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">COVID-19 information hub<\/a>, which it <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/25\/spotify-adds-fundraising-features-and-a-covid-19-news-hub-to-address-the-health-crisis\/\">added<\/a> in March 2020. TechCrunch asked Spotify how its app determines which podcast episodes address COVID-19 &#8212; it appears that the advisory shows up if words like &#8220;COVID-19,&#8221; &#8220;coronavirus&#8221; or &#8220;pandemic&#8221; appear in the metadata of an episode, including its title.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;On January 30, 2022, Spotify announced plans to add a content advisory to any podcast episode that includes a discussion about COVID-19. Three days later, on Feb 2, we launched the content advisory on our platform and we&#8217;ve been adding it to episodes that include discussion about COVID-19 on a rolling basis ever since. Today, the COVID content advisory appears on ~1.4 million podcast episodes on our platform,&#8221; a Spotify spokesperson said.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2290260\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Social platforms like Twitter acted faster in their attempts to combat the spread of COVID-19 misinformation. Just days after lockdowns in the U.S. began, Twitter <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/03\/18\/twitter-coronavirus-covid-19-misinformation-policy\/\">banned<\/a> any tweets that could help the virus spread. Two months later, it <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/11\/twitter-to-add-labels-and-warning-messages-to-disputed-and-misleading-covid-19-info\/\">released<\/a> a coronavirus advisory warning on tweets that may contain false information. Competing streaming services like Apple Podcasts don&#8217;t have these advisory warnings, though Apple Podcasts also doesn&#8217;t fund a podcaster who talks to right-wing conspiracy theorists for fun.<\/p>\n<p>Despite its PR nightmare, as calls to boycott Spotify trended across social media, the backlash did little to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/02\/spotify-backlash-over-joe-rogan-did-little-to-boost-its-streaming-rivals\/\">boost Spotify&#8217;s rivals<\/a>. Spotify remains dominant, though other platforms have begun to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/20\/spotify-subscription-numbers-up-youtube-music-tidal\/\">slowly chip away<\/a> at its lead.<\/p>\n<p><em>Update, 3\/28\/22, 9:20 PM ET with clarification from Spotify about the timeline of the feature rollout.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"zwBeaIbYQz\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/09\/spotify-rogan-saga-publisher-platform\/\">The Spotify-Rogan saga highlights the distinction between publishers and platforms<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;The Spotify-Rogan saga highlights the distinction between publishers and platforms&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/09\/spotify-rogan-saga-publisher-platform\/embed\/#?secret=P5GWz3ouCm#?secret=zwBeaIbYQz\" data-secret=\"zwBeaIbYQz\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>You probably remember a few months ago when you couldn&#8217;t turn on the news, check Twitter or talk to your conservative uncle without broaching the issue of Joe Rogan, who is signed to an exclusive deal with Spotify worth more than $200 million.
