lose sleep over Elon Musk&#8217;s desire to build the next Twitter"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Elon Musk tweeted this weekend that he is \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/elonmusk\/status\/1507907130124222471\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">giving serious thought<\/a>\u201d to building his own social media platform.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cGiven that Twitter serves as the de facto public town square, failing to adhere to free speech principles fundamentally undermines democracy,\u201d the billionaire serial entrepreneur who is CEO of Tesla and Space X <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/elonmusk\/status\/1507777261654605828\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tweeted<\/a>. \u201cWhat should be done?\u201d<\/p>\n<p>If your blood pressure spiked reading these tweets, you\u2019re not alone. But let\u2019s take a deep breath. We probably won\u2019t see an app called DogeSoci\u00e6lX any time soon.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289996\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Musk has a history of tweeting absurd memes, thoughts and even <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/09\/27\/tesla-ceo-elon-musk-responds-to-sec-securities-fraud-charges\/\">material information<\/a> about Tesla, then <a class=\"c-link\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/22\/us-regulators-say-someone-really-needs-to-monitor-elon-musks-tweets\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/22\/us-regulators-say-someone-really-needs-to-monitor-elon-musks-tweets\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\" data-remove-tab-index=\"true\">feigning shock<\/a> when U.S. regulators react with more than a raised eyebrow. <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">However, when it comes to Musk actually following through on his wacky Twitter ideas, his track record isn\u2019t great.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>This isn\u2019t the first time that Musk has fantasized publicly about his dreams of being the next Jack Dorsey (though maybe he\u2019s closer to a Zuck?).<\/p>\n<p>After journalists criticized Musk for his questionable Tesla management choices in 2018, he <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/elonmusk\/status\/999367582271422464\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">vowed<\/a> to launch a website called Pravda, the Russian word for \u201ctruth,\u201d which is also the name of an historic Russian communist newspaper. Musk\u2019s website would allow the public <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/05\/23\/elon-musk-has-a-very-bad-idea-for-a-website-rating-journalists\/\">to rate journalists<\/a>, editors and media outlets on their \u201ccore truth\u201d and \u201ccredibility scores.\u201d Thankfully, this idea did not come to fruition, but as all journalists know, Twitter already functions very well as a vehicle to make you aware when people don\u2019t agree with you.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Musk&#39;s sudden deep and genuine concern about Twitter&#39;s fairness &quot;as the de facto town square&quot; is just like his 2018 concerns about media accuracy\/objectivity: a deeply hypocritical ploy to shore up his (and his followers) absurd persecution fantasy. <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/cZIicOVTzb\">https:\/\/t.co\/cZIicOVTzb<\/a><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&mdash; E.W. Niedermeyer (@Tweetermeyer) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Tweetermeyer\/status\/1508103866599940104?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 27, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>When Musk\u2019s Twitter-borne ideas do get off the ground, they have traditionally fallen far short of becoming the next SpaceX.<\/p>\n<p>Also in 2018 \u2014 a big year for his antics \u2014 Musk announced his \u201cnew <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/elonmusk\/status\/973972643190792193\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">intergalactic media empire<\/a>,\u201d a comedy company called Thud (punctuated with an optional exclamation point). After Elon Musk was tapped to host SNL last year, I embarked on a Sisyphean journalistic <a href=\"https:\/\/www.mic.com\/p\/elon-musks-first-foray-into-comedy-was-a-strange-satirical-website-called-thud-77009671\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">task<\/a>: I contacted all 13 former employees of Thud, Musk\u2019s forgotten foray into comedy media.<\/p>\n<p>No one was willing to talk to me on the record. Powered by former editors of The Onion, Thud flopped, and was then reduced to a conversation starter on a resume (former Theranos employees <a href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@leonamarlene\/video\/7078315399233817899?_t=8R1ARWS97eg&amp;_r=1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">can relate<\/a>). It\u2019s no wonder that these writers and designers didn\u2019t want to revisit Thud, which its <a href=\"https:\/\/thud.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">minimalist website<\/a> now calls \u201cshort-lived\u201d and \u201captly named.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Initially, Musk funneled <a href=\"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2019\/7\/2\/18701197\/elon-musk-thud-satire-startup-onion-launch-failure\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$2 million<\/a> into Thud, but he left the company abruptly, leaving its editors with no plan to monetize the project.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cMaking a swift transition from being a billionaire-backed project to an independent media company is&#8230; You know,\u201d editor Cole Bolton <a href=\"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2019\/7\/2\/18701197\/elon-musk-thud-satire-startup-onion-launch-failure\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">told<\/a> The Verge at the time.<\/p>\n<p>Given his history of making outlandish statements online for the fun of it, there\u2019s little need to panic about Musk\u2019s sudden interest in creating a social media empire (this one isn&#8217;t even intergalactic!). Plus, even when there\u2019s a big name behind a new platform, there\u2019s no guarantee it\u2019ll take off. Donald Trump\u2019s own new app, Truth Social, may feel like it\u2019s poised to become a mainstream 4chan, but <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/21\/trumps-truth-social-app-launch-store-errors\/\">weeks after launch<\/a>, we\u2019re still 976,985th on the waitlist. And once you\u2019re admitted, the party doesn\u2019t appear to be too exciting (unless you&#8217;re into &#8220;<a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kelsaywhat\/status\/1508185434844766220\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">hot chicks golfing<\/a>&#8220;).<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">finally got off the waitlist for truth social <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/PaehCYfBTL\">pic.twitter.com\/PaehCYfBTL<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; kelsey weekman (@kelsaywhat) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kelsaywhat\/status\/1508185434844766220?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 27, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Even if Musk were to develop his own social media platform, he wouldn&#8217;t have the same level of reach he has on Twitter. He boasts 79.4 million followers, landing him solidly in the top 10 most-followed users on the site, beaten out only by figures like Barack Obama and Justin Bieber. But unlike Taylor Swift and Katy Perry, Musk leverages his following to make <a href=\"https:\/\/thehill.com\/homenews\/594711-elon-musk-blasted-for-tweeting-adolf-hitler-meme\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hitler jokes<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/elonmusk\/status\/1466074646240014340?s=20&amp;t=QAupCu5zirmbnsmrciOZZg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">compare<\/a> Twitter&#8217;s<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/03\/new-twitter-ceo-parag-agrawal-begins-restructuring-as-two-execs-step-down\/\"> new CEO Parag Agrawal<\/a> to Joseph Stalin. Notably, as Musk complains that he is not allowed to speak freely, these foul tweets were not removed by the platform; he <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2022\/02\/17\/elon-musk-tweet-hitler-meme-canada-freedom-convoy\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">deleted<\/a> his Hitler meme himself, and the dig at Agrawal is still up.<\/p>\n<p>This isn&#8217;t a free speech issue; it&#8217;s just Musk&#8217;s distaste for any form of regulation. It&#8217;s doubtful that Musk&#8217;s nearly 80 million followers would migrate over to his theoretical new platform, but even if they did, the SEC could still hold Musk accountable for whatever insider information he shares.<\/p>\n<p>Musk&#8217;s most powerful tool has always been Twitter, and like Trump, he doesn&#8217;t seem to gain anything by trying to start a new company that the SEC would still monitor anyway.<\/p>\n<p>This isn\u2019t to say that we shouldn\u2019t be concerned about the threat posed by egomaniacal men in power who are wealthy enough to make their fever dreams realities.<\/p>\n<p>After all, Musk seems to be a bit better at business than Trump. But sometimes, Musk\u2019s outbursts on Twitter do nothing but create polarizing, charged dialogue, and we forget that even though Musk&#8217;s tweets can move markets, sometimes, they simply just fall with a thud.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Elon Musk tweeted this weekend that he is \u201cgiving serious thought\u201d to building his own social media platform. of Tesla and Space X tweeted. \u201cWhat should be mpanies?tags=65745"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=65745"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=65745"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":193546312,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/theranos\/","name":"Theranos","slug":"theranos","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/193546312"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=193546312"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=193546312"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=193546312"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=193546312"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":599182,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/twitter\/","name":"Twitter","slug":"twitter","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/599182"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=599182"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=599182"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=599182"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=599182"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2289477,"date":"2022-03-25T10:12:46","date_gmt":"2022-03-25T17:12:46","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2289477"},"modified":"2022-03-25T10:28:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-25T17:28:42","slug":"hubspot-is-the-latest-saas-company-to-woo-creators","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/25\/hubspot-is-the-latest-saas-company-to-woo-creators\/","title":{"rendered":"HubSpot is the latest SaaS company to woo creators"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It&#8217;s getting harder these days to get your buyer&#8217;s attention. It used to be that you paid for some ads and threw up some blog posts and you were pretty much good to go, but as these channels become less effective, SaaS companies are looking to more <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/why-so-many-saas-companies-are-launching-their-own-media-operations\/\">sophisticated kinds of media production<\/a> to reach their intended audiences.<\/p>\n<p>This week, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.hubspot.com\/company-news\/hubspot-launches-new-hubspot-creators-program-to-invest-millions-in-emerging-talent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">HubSpot announced a program<\/a> to give creators some money and a platform to produce podcasts and deliver them on <a href=\"https:\/\/www.hubspot.com\/creators\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the HubSpot website<\/a>. The company hopes to take advantage of having access to a wider variety of content while giving the creators a way to reach a broader audience.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Breaking through in the saturated podcast market can be incredibly difficult, especially for creators who are starting from scratch,&#8221; Kieran Flanagan, SVP of Marketing at HubSpot, said <a href=\"https:\/\/www.hubspot.com\/company-news\/hubspot-launches-new-hubspot-creators-program-to-invest-millions-in-emerging-talent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in a post<\/a> announcing the news. &#8220;Through HubSpot Creators, we\u2019re able to leverage our position as a leader in the content space to raise the profiles of emerging creators who share in our mission of helping millions of organizations grow better.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289477\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>In addition to getting access to the company&#8217;s platform and potential wider reach, creators get a monthly payment that increases as the audience grows. HubSpot has created four growth stages that correspond to venture funding notions: seed and Series A, B and C. They can also get access to other resources like editors and producers as they move through this system.<\/p>\n<p>Brent Leary, founder and principal analyst at CRM Essentials, believes the approach is a really smart move.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Embracing creators and helping them to tell their stories allows HubSpot to extend their content ecosystem but also be a part of the broader creator ecosystem. That approach can allow HubSpot to build important relationships with individuals and communities as they evolve their own content strategy into other formats and channels,&#8221; Leary told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>HubSpot was born as an inbound marketing platform in 2006, using blogs to drive interest in a company&#8217;s products and services. While the content marketing idea has evolved, Flanagan wrote <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/feed\/update\/urn:li:activity:6912753134855430145\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in a post on LinkedIn<\/a> announcing the new program that the original inbound marketing idea still resonates and has increased in importance with the development of product-led growth.<\/p>\n<p>Another big element here is building communities &#8212; people who matter to you as a brand &#8212; around these content pieces. Flanagan said that communities create a way to drive even more interest either directly (a percentage of these people become customers) or indirectly (they at least share your content with a broader world).<\/p>\n<p>The company is launching the program with eight podcasts with names like &#8220;<a href=\"https:\/\/listen.hubspot.com\/public\/83\/Content-Is-Profit-7b15f1b3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Content is Profit&#8221;<\/a> and &#8220;<a href=\"https:\/\/listen.hubspot.com\/public\/83\/(un)sexy-692b20fc\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">(Un)Sexy<\/a>.&#8221; These podcast themes relate in some way to HubSpot&#8217;s mission as a sales and marketing platform, offering content that HubSpot hopes will drive interest in its products and services.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s worth noting that HubSpot isn&#8217;t alone in creating programs like this. LinkedIn <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/pulse\/meet-first-class-linkedins-creator-accelerator-program-andrei-santalo\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">offers a similar approach<\/a> for creators,<a href=\"https:\/\/mailchimp.com\/presents\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> as does MailChimp<\/a>. But is piggybacking on these platforms the best way for creators to build an audience? What are the trade-offs?<\/p>\n<p>Per a non-public creator terms sheet provided to TechCrunch by a source, HubSpot will pay creators a minimum of $1,000 per month for creating their weekly podcast, regardless of how many downloads it gets. This seems like a good deal for new podcasters, since it can take a while to get an independent show to the point where it is generating that much income. Podcasters in this lowest \u201cseed\u201d tier are also given a one-time marketing investment of $5,000.<\/p>\n<p>But podcasters must give up some rights for access to this fast infusion of cash. Per HubSpot\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/legal.hubspot.com\/hubspot-creators-program-agreement\">public creator program agreement<\/a>, participation in the program grants HubSpot a perpetual license to their show, including altering it and creating derivative works from it. If HubSpot deems a host unable to fulfill their obligations, HubSpot reserves the right to replace them.<\/p>\n<p>Though creators remain the owners of their show, HubSpot\u2019s perpetual license makes it clear that this financial support comes with strings attached.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cHubSpot respects the rights of creators, and they believe this strikes a fair balance between creators and HubSpot,\u201d a HubSpot spokesperson told TechCrunch. \u201cHubSpot will also consider waiving exclusivity for creators who leave the program in good standing.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>LinkedIn also recently launched a similar podcast network but declined to share specifics about its creator agreement. A LinkedIn representative told TechCrunch that its podcast partners \u201cretain complete ownership over their content,\u201d but did not elaborate on its licensing agreement.<\/p>\n<p>But as more SaaS companies launch their own podcast networks, podcasters will face difficult decisions regarding the value of their creative control versus the access to funding that these programs provide.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mxfn4521xf\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/why-so-many-saas-companies-are-launching-their-own-media-operations\/\">Why so many SaaS companies are launching their own media operations<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Why so many SaaS companies are launching their own media operations&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/why-so-many-saas-companies-are-launching-their-own-media-operations\/embed\/#?secret=35y4SSdse4#?secret=mxfn4521xf\" data-secret=\"mxfn4521xf\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>It&#8217;s getting harder these days to get your buyer&#8217;s attention. It used to be that you paid for some ads and threw up some blog posts and you were pretty much good to go, but as these channels become less effective, SaaS companies are looking to more sophisticated kinds of media production to reach their will list NYC taxis to combat driver shortage and high fares"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">If you can&#8217;t disrupt them, join them? Once poised to render the taxi system obsolete, Uber <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/uber-reaches-deal-to-list-all-new-york-city-taxis-on-its-app-11648123201\">reached an agreement<\/a> to list all New York City taxis on its app. Later this spring, New York City riders will be able to hail a cab right from their Uber apps, helping the company combat its driver shortage and rising fares.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Our partnerships with the taxi industry look different around the world and as we look at the next five years, we strongly believe that there is no world in which taxis and Uber exist separately,&#8221; Uber spokesperson Conor Ferguson told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;There is just too much to gain for both sides. Taxis help us unlock new markets. In fact, it\u2019s now our primary product in places like Hong Kong and Turkey.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The partnership works by integrating Uber&#8217;s software with existing taxi software from companies like CMT and Curb, which run in 14,000 New York City taxis.\u00a0According to reports from <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/uber-reaches-deal-to-list-all-new-york-city-taxis-on-its-app-11648123201\">the Wall Street Journal<\/a>, taxi fares via Uber will be the around the same price as a generic Uber X. Cab drivers who pick up Uber passengers will be paid the same rate as standard Uber drivers &#8212; their payment is determined by a minimum time and distance rate. But Uber uses different metrics to calculate pay than taxis. So, taxi drivers will be able to see their expected earnings before accepting an Uber passenger, a courtesy that Uber doesn&#8217;t extend to its existing drivers. Uber takes about<a href=\"https:\/\/investor.uber.com\/news-events\/news\/press-release-details\/2022\/Uber-Announces-Results-for-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2021\/\"> 20% of fares<\/a>, according to its investor reports, but Uber has not disclosed the terms of its deal with the New York City Taxi and Limousine Commission, like what kind of cut will be deducted from taxi rides.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289048\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Taxi drivers around the world have <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/08\/02\/spanish-anti-uber-taxi-strike-ends-after-government-agrees-new-regulation\/\">protested<\/a> the prevalence of ride share businesses like Uber. In France, the company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2014\/02\/28\/uber-wants-to-take-over-the-french-market-by-using-dumping-tactics\/?_ga=2.126779973.916687417.1647871065-2083850299.1647286359\">once operated at a loss<\/a> to lure customers and drivers away from existing infrastructure. This overall model of <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/12\/will-ride-hailing-profits-ever-come\/\">accruing debt<\/a> to keep prices low continued until the company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/04\/uber-squeaks-tiny-adjust\">managed<\/a> a small profit in Q3 2021, despite still losing $2.4 billion dollars. The decision to work with taxi drivers has <a href=\"https:\/\/asia.nikkei.com\/Asia300\/Uber-strikes-taxi-partnership-in-Thailand-seventh-deal-in-Asia\">proven successful<\/a> overseas &#8212; Uber has partnerships with taxi providers in countries like Spain, Colombia, Austria, Germany, South Korea and more &#8212; so it&#8217;s no wonder that the company will try this in one of its biggest U.S. markets.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ueqykazssC\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/uber-boosts-q1-profit-guidance-as-the-world-gets-moving-again\/\">Uber boosts Q1 profit guidance as the world gets moving again<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Uber boosts Q1 profit guidance as the world gets moving again&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/uber-boosts-q1-profit-guidance-as-the-world-gets-moving-again\/embed\/#?secret=4rSzLCw4Ay#?secret=ueqykazssC\" data-secret=\"ueqykazssC\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you can&#8217;t disrupt them, join them? Once poised to render the taxi system obsolete, Uber reached an agreement to list all New York City taxis on its app. Later this spring, New York City riders will be able to hail a cab right from their Uber apps, helping the company combat its driver shortage can now make GIFs in Twitter&#8217;s iOS app"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">If you ever wanted to make a GIF from your iOS camera while using the Twitter app, today&#8217;s your lucky day. Twitter <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/TwitterSupport\/status\/1506346203310612490\">announced<\/a> that now, we can do just that.<\/p>\n<p>When you compose a new tweet on iOS, click the camera button. Then, you have the option to choose between a photo, a video and an animated GIF. Your GIF recording can&#8217;t be very long &#8212; only a few seconds &#8212; but hey, it&#8217;ll probably come in handy once or twice?<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Ok GIFs aren\u2019t new but what *is new* is the option to capture your own using the in-app camera on iOS. <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/3Hl6q78e6s\">pic.twitter.com\/3Hl6q78e6s<\/a><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287999\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>&mdash; Twitter Support (@TwitterSupport) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/TwitterSupport\/status\/1506346203310612490?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 22, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>After you record your short GIF, you have the option to either play it front to back on loop, or you can make it play like an Instagram boomerang, playing forward, then reverse on loop. The world is your oyster, unless if you want to make a GIF that lasts longer than like two seconds.<\/p>\n<p>Once you make the GIF, it saves automatically to your camera roll as a GIF in your images folder &#8212; it&#8217;s not a video. Because it&#8217;s a GIF.<\/p>\n<p>Twitter releases so many new features these days that it&#8217;s hard to keep track. Some recent updates you may have missed include posting <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/18\/twitter-clipping-spaces\/\">clips from Spaces<\/a>, a potential upcoming spin on Instagram&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/twitters-spin-on-the-close-friends-story-might-be-on-its-way-soon\/\">&#8220;close friends&#8221; list<\/a> and some <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/10\/twitters-latest-update-makes-it-easier-to-escape-its-recommendation-algorithm\/\">timeline algorithm<\/a> snafus. Twitter hasn&#8217;t indicated when this GIF feature might roll out for Android, but Twitter usually <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/20\/twitter-is-rolling-out-its-communities-feature-to-all-android-users\/\">adds in<\/a> new updates to Android users eventually. the zoo in Zoom with these horrific 3D animatars"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A picture\u2019s worth a thousand words, but this image of Zoom\u2019s newest feature can be summed up in just one: what?<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/zoom\/\">Zoom<\/a> is introducing a feature today that lets you show up to your work meetings as a bunny rabbit (or a dog, a fox, a panda, a horse \u2014 you get the point). The Avatars feature recognizes the shape of your eyes, nose and mouth to mirror your head movements and facial expressions, but Zoom is quick to note in its announcement that the feature does not use facial recognition, nor does it store biometric data. That would\u2019ve really put them in the <em>dog house<\/em>.<\/p>\n<p>These avatars are intended to give the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/21\/this-is-your-brain-on-zoom\/\">Zoom fatigued<\/a> among us a way to communicate body language and facial expressions without actually appearing on camera. On the flip side, imagine you\u2019re a high school teacher and you log on to teach, but instead you find a sea of 25 bunny rabbits staring back blankly at you as though you\u2019re a character in a pandemic-era reimagining of \u201cDonnie Darko.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287712\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Avatars will be available on both Windows and macOS desktop devices, as well as iOS mobile devices, so long as you\u2019re running Zoom version 5.10.0 or higher (sorry, Android users who want to be horses). To <a href=\"https:\/\/support.zoom.us\/hc\/en-us\/articles\/4642184011917\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">use the feature<\/a>, click the caret (^) symbol next to the start\/stop video button. If you select either the \u201cChoose Virtual Background\u201d or \u201cChoose Video Filter\u201d option, you\u2019ll see a tab that says \u201cAvatars,\u201d which will help you complete your inter-species transformation.<\/p>\n<p>Avatars are compatible with virtual backgrounds. Importantly, your talking animal avatar can wear either a hoodie or a t-shirt.<\/p>\n<p>At launch, animals are the only avatars available, but it\u2019s easy to imagine other kinds of avatars that might get added (putting this completely unfounded prediction in writing now: Zoom partners with Universal Pictures, your boss turns into a Minion).<\/p>\n<p>Zoom suggests that this feature may be useful for virtual pediatric appointments, children&#8217;s science classes or \u201c[breaking] the ice during virtual events.&#8221; That last one might be a stretch. But if Zoom wants to cure our Zoom fatigue as we enter year two of a global pandemic, we have a few suggestions for how to spice things up:<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<ul>\n<li>Incorporate a voice modulator. Intimidate your colleagues by speaking to them as though you&#8217;re Darth Vader.<\/li>\n<li>Gamify Zoom by adding points. What do the points do for you? I don&#8217;t know, I&#8217;m not a product designer.<\/li>\n<li>Add an HP bar to time-limited Zoom rooms. culture","slug":"internet-culture","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/76373"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=76373"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=76373"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=76373"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=76373"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2287439,"date":"2022-03-22T05:00:04","date_gmt":"2022-03-22T12:00:04","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287439"},"modified":"2022-03-22T07:59:55","modified_gmt":"2022-03-22T14:59:55","slug":"apple-podcasts-followers-subscription-features","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/22\/apple-podcasts-followers-subscription-features\/","title":{"rendered":"Podcasters, get ready to find out how many followers you have on Apple Podcasts"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Apple Podcasts is<a href=\"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/3142-march-2022-creator-updates\"> rolling out<\/a> new features to incentivize podcasters to offer <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/15\/apple-podcasts-subscriptions-go-live-worldwide\/\">paid subscriptions<\/a> to listeners on the app. One of those features will &#8212; for better or for worse &#8212; reveal to podcasters in their private analytics dashboard how many people follow them on Apple Podcasts. Get ready for an ego check!<\/p>\n<p>For whatever reason, follower counts haven&#8217;t been visible to creators, though the Apple Podcasts Connect page has shown stats about how many listeners you have, how long people listen before dropping off and how different episodes perform compared to one another.<\/p>\n<p>Some podcasters might notice that their stats on Apple Podcasts Connect are lower than expected, though. The <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/27\/spotify-says-u-s-podcast-listeners-now-use-its-service-more-than-apple-podcasts\/\">majority of U.S. podcast listeners use Spotify<\/a>, so these analytics, which only show Apple Podcasts listenership, don&#8217;t offer creators a holistic picture of their show&#8217;s performance (however, the drop-off rate can be useful information, since that data point isn&#8217;t available on distribution platforms like Libsyn).<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287439\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;Listeners who follow a show want to receive new episodes as they become available, so a show\u2019s followers can serve as an indicator for those likely to subscribe,&#8221; Apple wrote in <a href=\"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/3142-march-2022-creator-updates\">a blog post.<\/a><\/p>\n<p>By Apple&#8217;s logic, if you notice that you have a lot of followers on their app, you might consider launching paywalled content through their subscription service, which <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/15\/apple-podcasts-subscriptions-go-live-worldwide\/\">launched<\/a> less than a year ago. Podcasters hosting exclusive, subscriber-only content agree to pay Apple a 30% cut of their subscription revenue in year one, followed by 15% in year two. But for those who release <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/27\/spotify-launches-paid-podcasts-through-new-anchor-feature\/\">paywalled content on Spotify<\/a>, the platform currently isn&#8217;t taking a revenue cut, and after two years after its launch, it will take 5%. Other podcasters may choose to monetize their shows in a different way entirely by creating fan memberships on platforms like Patreon, which may include access to private Discord servers that help cultivate a community around a show, as opposed to just offering platform-specific bonus content.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2287473\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2287473\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2287473\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?w=680\" alt=\"A screenshot of Apple Podcasts' analytics dashboard\" width=\"680\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png 2640w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=150,113 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=300,226 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=768,578 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=680,512 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=1536,1155 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=2048,1541 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Apple-Podcasts-Connect-Followers.png?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2287473\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple Podcasts<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>But Apple&#8217;s advantage is that its app comes pre-downloaded on your iPhone, so newer podcast listeners may find it easier to subscribe to a show on an app they already have. Apple is so eager to get a chunk of podcasters&#8217; revenue that it&#8217;s launching Jump Start, a program that offers podcasters direct guidance from the Apple Podcasts team to develop their subscription offerings. But this guidance is only available to members of the Apple Podcasters Program &#8212; people who have already opted into selling a subscription on Apple Podcasts by paying a $19.99 annual fee.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>A few more minor updates for those enrolled in the program: Now, you can upload .mp3 files as subscriber-only audio (previously, you could only upload .wav and .flac), and you can customize the subscription banner that appears on your show.<\/p>\n<p>All updates will roll out today, except for that tantalizing follower count, which will appear on creators&#8217; Apple Podcasts Connect dashboards next month.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Apple Podcasts is rolling out new features to incentivize podcasters to offer paid subscriptions to listeners on the app. One of those features will &#8212; for better or for worse &#8212; reveal to podcasters in their private analytics dashboard how many people follow them on Apple Podcasts. Get ready for an ego check! /techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=523"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=523"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=523"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=523"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2287306,"date":"2022-03-21T13:17:56","date_gmt":"2022-03-21T20:17:56","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2287306"},"modified":"2022-03-21T13:41:00","modified_gmt":"2022-03-21T20:41:00","slug":"grubhub-lawsuit-hidden-fees-dc-attorney-general-disclosure","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/grubhub-lawsuit-hidden-fees-dc-attorney-general-disclosure\/","title":{"rendered":"Lawsuit prompts Grubhub to add disclosures about hidden fees"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Washington D.C. Attorney General Karl Racine <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/AGKarlRacine\/status\/1505913724913209348\">announced<\/a> today that his office filed a lawsuit against Grubhub for &#8220;misleading District residents and taking advantage of local restaurants to boost its own profits.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https:\/\/oag.dc.gov\/sites\/default\/files\/2022-03\/2022-03-21-Grubhub-Complaint-.pdf\">lawsuit<\/a> alleges that Grubhub violated D.C.&#8217;s Consumer Protection Procedures Act (CPPA) in eight different ways, which mostly center on false advertising. The filing references misleading prices (prices are often higher in-app than at the restaurant) and false claims that deliveries via Grubhub+ were free when they still contained a service charge.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">NEW: We&#39;re suing Grubhub for misleading District residents and taking advantage of local restaurants to boost its own profits.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287306\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Grubhub charges hidden fees and uses bait-and-switch tactics, all while pretending to help local businesses during the pandemic. This needs to stop.<\/p>\n<p>&mdash; AG Karl A. Racine (@AGKarlRacine) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/AGKarlRacine\/status\/1505913724913209348?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 21, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Some of the complaints point to practices that the platform has since discontinued, like Grubhub&#8217;s early-pandemic-era &#8220;<\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/05\/its-time-to-stop-using-grubhub-seamless-forever\/\">Supper for Support<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">&#8221; promotion. Launched in late March 2020, Grubhub offered restaurants the opportunity to offer a $10 coupon on orders over $30, but the restaurant had to foot the bill for that free food. On the consumer end, Grubhub encouraged customers to &#8220;save while supporting the restaurants [they] love,&#8221; even though their promotion actually put more strain on restaurants by pressuring them to lower profit margins (if one neighborhood taco shop enrolled in the promotion, and the other didn&#8217;t, where do you think consumers would direct their business?). <\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The company deceived users with a promotion that claimed to support local restaurants during the heart of the pandemic. But in reality, this program cut into struggling restaurants\u2019 profit margins while padding Grubhub\u2019s bottom line,&#8221; Attorney General Racine said in a statement.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Grubhub is also being sued for listing restaurants on its website and app that weren&#8217;t registered with Grubhub, making websites for affiliated restaurants without their permission and listing phone numbers on restaurant pages that directed to Grubhub representatives, rather than the actual restaurant. Grubhub has also since stopped those practices, perhaps in part due to a past <a href=\"https:\/\/www.foodandwine.com\/news\/grubhub-class-action-lawsuit-adding-restaurants-without-permission\">lawsuit<\/a> over Grubhub listing restaurants without their permission.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">We all deserve to make informed decisions about where and how we spend our dollars\u2014and that\u2019s what we\u2019re fighting for in our new lawsuit against Grubhub.<\/p>\n<p>Here are just some of the deceptive practices Grubhub uses, taking advantage of DC residents and restaurants.\u2b07\ufe0f <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/87oICD4NXl\">pic.twitter.com\/87oICD4NXl<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; AG Karl A. Racine (@AGKarlRacine) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/AGKarlRacine\/status\/1505951068848590855?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 21, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>In an emailed statement, a company spokesperson said: \u201cWe are disappointed [the Attorney General&#8217;s office] have moved forward with this lawsuit because our practices have always complied with D.C. law, and in any event, many of the practices at issue have been discontinued. We will aggressively defend our business in court and look forward to continuing to serve D.C. restaurants and diners.\u201d The spokesperson added that Grubhub has worked with Racine&#8217;s office over the last year to address their concerns.<\/p>\n<p>As a result of the lawsuit, a Grubhub spokesperson told TechCrunch that the app will make some messaging changes on its app, which extend to all users, not just D.C. customers. Now, Grubhub will include a disclosure during checkout that prices may be lower in store. Instead of advertising Grubhub+ to offer unlimited free delivery, the company will be more transparent about the actual offer, which provides $0 delivery on orders over $12, though service fees may apply. Grubhub will also make it more clear that customers can place free orders online, but that this only applies if you&#8217;re picking up the food.<\/p>\n<p>Despite an uptick in delivery orders during the pandemic, food delivery apps have still <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/doordash-and-uber-eats-are-hot-theyre-still-not-making-money-11622194203\">struggled<\/a> to turn a profit \u2014 even as their business model leaves many gig workers and local restaurant owners with the short end of the stick.<\/p>\n<p>Those inequities are increasingly attracting the attention of state and federal regulators. Attorney General Racine&#8217;s office has a history of suing delivery apps for deceptive practices. In 2019, Racine <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/11\/19\/doordash-tipping-practices-prompts-lawsuit-from-dc-attorney-general\/\">sued DoorDash<\/a> for using customer tips to pay delivery drivers&#8217; base wages, depriving drivers of their full tips. A year later, DoorDash was fined $2.5 million, which included $1.5 million to be paid to D.C. workers.<\/p>\n<p><iframe id=\"doc_58746\" class=\"scribd_iframe_embed\" title=\"D.C. Attorney General's Office lawsuit against Grubhub, March 2022\" src=\"https:\/\/www.scribd.com\/embeds\/565912050\/content?start_page=1&amp;view_mode=scroll&amp;access_key=key-5OeChvOaEqZ0c26xUD01\" width=\"100%\" height=\"600\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\" data-auto-height=\"false\" data-aspect-ratio=\"0.75\"><\/iframe><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"3A1LbSKQGy\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/05\/its-time-to-stop-using-grubhub-seamless-forever\/\">GrubHub\/Seamless&#8217;s pandemic initiatives are predatory and exploitative, and it&#8217;s time to stop using them<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;GrubHub\/Seamless&#8217;s pandemic initiatives are predatory and exploitative, and it&#8217;s time to stop using them&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/05\/its-time-to-stop-using-grubhub-seamless-forever\/embed\/#?secret=cdNM5kh5gQ#?secret=3A1LbSKQGy\" data-secret=\"3A1LbSKQGy\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Pud93NAotV\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/11\/19\/doordash-tipping-practices-prompts-lawsuit-from-dc-attorney-general\/\">DoorDash tipping practices prompts lawsuit from DC Attorney General<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;DoorDash tipping practices prompts lawsuit from DC Attorney General&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/11\/19\/doordash-tipping-practices-prompts-lawsuit-from-dc-attorney-general\/embed\/#?secret=UxsT8mmW2L#?secret=Pud93NAotV\" data-secret=\"Pud93NAotV\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Washington D.C. is paywalling the ability to upload NSFW photos"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Flickr isn&#8217;t very good at making money, but as the old adage goes, sex sells. So, in <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">an attempt to draw in more paying subscribers, Flickr changed its content guidelines to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.flickrhelp.com\/hc\/en-us\/articles\/4404064374164-Set-the-Safety-Levels-of-Your-Flickr-Content-or-Account\">only <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.flickrhelp.com\/hc\/en-us\/articles\/4404064374164-Set-the-Safety-Levels-of-Your-Flickr-Content-or-Account\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">allow<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> Flickr Pro users to post &#8220;restricted&#8221; or &#8220;moderate&#8221; content, which includes photos of &#8220;full-frontal nudity and sexual acts.&#8221;\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Honestly, it&#8217;s not a bad move &#8212; it might be more effective than <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/19\/flickr-owner-smugmug-emails-subscribers-with-an-urgent-request-help-us-find-more-paying-users\/\">asking subscribers<\/a> to recruit their friends to pay for Flickr.<\/p>\n<p>When SmugMug <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/04\/20\/smugmug-acquires-flickr\/\">acquired<\/a> the photo-hosting service in 2018, CEO Don MacAskill hoped to make the service profitable, calling it \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/www.usatoday.com\/story\/tech\/2018\/04\/20\/smugmug-buys-flickr-verizon-oath\/537377002\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">core to the entire fabric of the Internet<\/a>.\u201d But this wasn&#8217;t just hyperbolic CEO-speak &#8212; MacAskill had a point. Flickr is a historical archive. For one thing, it showcases actual historical images, but it also chronicles a visual history of the world through the lens of millions of people since 2004. It would be sad if that were all to disappear.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286324\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>But Flickr is very expensive to run because it hosts so much data on the internet. For a while, there wasn&#8217;t much of a reason to pay for Flickr, since all users had a free terabyte of storage for their photos. But under SmugMug&#8217;s management, Flickr instituted a limit on how many photos free users could store, knocking down that terabyte of data to just 1,000 photos. Flickr also warned users that after a certain date, their photos <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/02\/05\/flickr-deleting-photos-how-to-backup\/\">could be deleted<\/a>. These major changes were implemented to encourage users to save their personal archives by upgrading to a paid plan.<\/p>\n<p>So far, Flickr <a href=\"https:\/\/blog.flickr.net\/en\/2022\/03\/17\/flickr-forever-2022\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said<\/a> it hasn&#8217;t actually deleted any uploads (thank you, Flickr, but also, this means I wasted an afternoon in 2019 downloading zip files of everything I ever posted). But it&#8217;s still not making money, hence the pivot to inviting NSFW uploads.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">&#8220;Photographers who craft and create work that might be considered risqu\u00e9 by some will have a safe place online to interact with one another, share mutual interests, and put their art into the world without the fear of it being removed or them being banned entirely from the communities they love,&#8221; Head of Flickr Alex Seville wrote in a <\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/blog.flickr.net\/en\/2022\/03\/17\/flickr-forever-2022\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">blog post<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">. &#8220;<\/span><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">But we\u2019ve been lax in truly defining a space for these photographers, until now.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p>In less sexy news, Flickr is continuing to limit what users can do with their free accounts. Today&#8217;s announcement also states that now, free users can only post 50 non-public photos.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;We love being entrusted with your photos &#8212; but we love seeing them get discovered, added to groups and submitted to photo competitions even more,&#8221; Seville explained. &#8220;We\u2019d never turn you away if you just want a safe place to store a lifetime\u2019s worth of images, you\u2019ll just need a Pro membership to do so.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Flickr says it will keep free users updated about how and when these updates will affect their accounts. But this market Flickr is targeting to boost its subscription revenue is a very specific one: people who upload private photos (but no more than 1,000 of them) and NSFW photographers. Here&#8217;s to hoping that nude photography can save this slice of the internet.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"1UyLSAiTsE\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/19\/flickr-owner-smugmug-emails-subscribers-with-an-urgent-request-help-us-find-more-paying-users\/\">Flickr owner SmugMug emails subscribers with an urgent request: help us find more paying users<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Flickr owner SmugMug emails subscribers with an urgent request: help us find more paying users&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/19\/flickr-owner-smugmug-emails-subscribers-with-an-urgent-request-help-us-find-more-paying-users\/embed\/#?secret=aVRcL89rE9#?secret=1UyLSAiTsE\" data-secret=\"1UyLSAiTsE\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Flickr isn&#8217;t very good at making money, but as the old adage goes, sex sells. includes photos of &#8220;full-frontal nudity and sexual acts.&#8221;\u00a0 Honestly, it&#8217;s not a web","slug":"world-wide-web","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/2648"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=2648"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2285957,"date":"2022-03-17T06:34:19","date_gmt":"2022-03-17T13:34:19","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285957"},"modified":"2022-03-17T07:54:29","modified_gmt":"2022-03-17T14:54:29","slug":"tiktok-stories-expanded-pilot-feature","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/tiktok-stories-expanded-pilot-feature\/","title":{"rendered":"TikTok is expanding the pilot of its Stories feature"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">TikTok is expanding the pilot of its Stories feature, which the platform <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/04\/tiktok-confirms-pilot-test-of-tiktok-stories-is-now-underway\/\">previously confirmed<\/a> was in testing last summer.<\/p>\n<p>Like an Instagram story, TikTok Stories last for 24 hours before they are automatically deleted, and they can be viewed by navigating to a user&#8217;s profile and clicking their profile picture. Stories also seem to be appearing on the For You page. As the poster, you can see how many people viewed your story, but unlike Instagram, you can&#8217;t see who viewed it. But, you can like a story and leave a public comment, whereas on Instagram, commenters can only reply to the poster directly in a private message.<\/p>\n<p>To post a story, click the &#8220;post&#8221; button on the bottom center navigation bar of the app. Then, you can scroll to a &#8220;quick&#8221; camera mode, which lets you post a photo or a video to your story. These videos have the same creation options as normal TikTok videos, allowing you to reply to comments, use filters and more. Photos don&#8217;t have quite the same functionality &#8212; you don&#8217;t need a recording timer for a photo, since, you know, it&#8217;s a photo &#8212; but you can still add music and effects to photos.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285957\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285965\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285965\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2285965\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?w=314\" alt=\"TikTok Stories\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png 1170w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=69,150 69w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=139,300 139w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=768,1662 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=314,680 314w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=710,1536 710w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=946,2048 946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/IMG_2131.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285965\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> TikTok; screenshot by TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Not all users will have access to this feature yet. From our testing, it appears that if you don&#8217;t have the feature, you can&#8217;t see stories that users with the feature have uploaded. We gained access to the feature from our U.S.-based account, but <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Lauren9Dudley\/status\/1504409155758657538\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">users in the U.K.<\/a> have also reported access to stories.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Currently, we&#8217;re expanding a pilot test, which provides creators with additional formats to bring their creative ideas to life for the TikTok community,&#8221; a TikTok spokesperson confirmed to TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p><em>This story is developing&#8230;<\/em><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/TikTok?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#TikTok<\/a> is now showing the story in the profile just like Instagram \ud83d\ude05 <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/bCGBQHdd9e\">pic.twitter.com\/bCGBQHdd9e<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; button","slug":"like-button","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/19740455"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=19740455"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=19740455"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=19740455"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=19740455"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":581,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/software\/","name":"Software","slug":"software","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/581"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=581"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=581"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=581"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=581"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":5938293,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/tiktok\/","name":"tiktok","slug":"tiktok","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/5938293"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=5938293"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=5938293"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=5938293"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=5938293"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":272240,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/video-hosting\/","name":"video hosting","slug":"video-hosting","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/272240"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=272240"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=272240"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=272240"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=272240"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2285752,"date":"2022-03-17T06:03:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-17T13:03:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2285752"},"modified":"2022-03-17T13:36:58","modified_gmt":"2022-03-17T20:36:58","slug":"dorian-interactive-storytelling-fan-fiction","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/dorian-interactive-storytelling-fan-fiction\/","title":{"rendered":"Dorian&#8217;s no-code, interactive storytelling app turns fiction writers into game developers"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As an interactive storytelling platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/home.dorian.live\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dorian<\/a> is building a new way for writers to make money off of their fiction by turning their tales into choose-your-own-adventure mobile games. As users navigate the free-to-play app, they can spend in-app currency to unlock alternative story routes, directly putting a cut of the payment in the author\u2019s pocket.<\/p>\n<p>Today, Dorian announced that it raised a $14 million Series A round led by the Raine Group with participation from March Gaming, VGames, Gaingels, Graham &amp; Walker and London Venture Partners, where Dorian co-founder and CEO Julia Palatovska was once an investor. Before that, she spent seven years at G5 Games, where she was Head of Business Development &amp; Licensing.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI spent about two years investing in some early-stage startups, and I was very inspired and itching to go back into building, which is how the idea for Dorian came together,\u201d Palatovska told TechCrunch. \u201cI think the biggest inspiration and the idea here is, how can we enable more people to participate in the games industry?\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285752\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5Mn9lKnkA8\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/10\/6-technologists-discuss-how-no-code-tools-are-changing-software-development\/\">6 technologists discuss how no-code tools are changing software development<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;6 technologists discuss how no-code tools are changing software development&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/10\/6-technologists-discuss-how-no-code-tools-are-changing-software-development\/embed\/#?secret=Tw9iNdouQv#?secret=5Mn9lKnkA8\" data-secret=\"5Mn9lKnkA8\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Available on <a href=\"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/dorian-the-future-of-fiction\/id1529215455?_branch_match_id=864551617862601586&amp;_branch_referrer=H4sIAAAAAAAAA8soKSkottLXT8kvykzM00ssKNDLyczL1g8I9XeuMonw8ctJAgCvvFRvIwAAAA%3D%3D&amp;utm_campaign=episode%20sharing&amp;utm_medium=share&amp;utm_source=app\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">iOS<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/play.google.com\/store\/apps\/details?gl=US&amp;hl=en_US&amp;id=com.dorian.playtogether\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Android<\/a>, the no-code app allows anyone to turn their stories into interactive games, even if they have no experience with game design. Instead of publishing a short story, where writers are usually awarded a flat fee (or no pay at all, for smaller markets), Dorian offers a more continuous revenue stream. But the trade-off is that nothing is guaranteed, especially on an emerging platform.<\/p>\n<p>But Palatovska is optimistic about Dorian\u2019s potential to support creatives.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe have around 250 monetizing creators, and that\u2019s growing quite fast compared to most creator platforms, where it takes years to start monetizing,\u201d she told TechCrunch. \u201cI think that\u2019s exciting in light of this round, because we can reach significantly more creators, and fans who will be willing to support them. In terms of revenue, top creators are currently making around $15,000 in annualized revenue. We have a couple of creators who already started making Dorian their full time job, and this is just the beginning.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285861\" style=\"width: 636px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285861\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2285861\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Dorian-Updated-2.png?w=626\" alt=\"\" width=\"626\" height=\"592\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Dorian-Updated-2.png 626w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Dorian-Updated-2.png?resize=150,142 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Dorian-Updated-2.png?resize=300,284 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Dorian-Updated-2.png?resize=50,47 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 626px) 100vw, 626px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285861\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Dorian<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Dorian is similar to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2014\/02\/20\/pocket-gems-launches-episode\/\">Episode<\/a>, a viral interactive storytelling app produced by Pocket Gems. But on Episode, in order to monetize, writers need to accumulate at least 500,000 reads in a 60-day period, which is no easy feat. Dorian has no readership requirements before a creator can start monetizing. Any user over the age of 13 can monetize on Dorian through <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/08\/accounts-payable-automation-startup-tipalti-raises-270m-quadruples-valuation-to-8-3b\/\">Tipalti<\/a>, the same payout provider that Twitch and Roblox use.<\/p>\n<p>When a reader makes an in-app purchase to follow a paywalled route on a story, the payment is split 50-50 between Dorian and the author. But Dorian is different from other platforms (and the online fan fiction market more broadly) because creators are encouraged to make fan works from stories that already exist on Dorian. This is because of the creator agreement that writers sign before publishing a story on Dorian \u2014 writers retain their own IP, Palatovska said, but they can also give permission for their stories to be iterated upon by other users.<\/p>\n<p>Fan-fiction writers tend to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/26\/inside-realms-of-ruin-ya-novelists-failed-nft-project\/\">be on high alert<\/a> any time monetization of their works is brought up. Last year, Tumblr users lashed out against the platform because they suggested that bloggers might <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/22\/tumblr-community-lash-out-post-plus-subscription\/\">paywall their fan art<\/a> with its new subscription feature. Fan creators can also be skeptical because, historically, they&#8217;ve been exploited.<\/p>\n<p>In 2006, a platform called FanLib raised <a href=\"https:\/\/www.crunchbase.com\/organization\/fanlib\/company_financials\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$3 million<\/a> in venture capital to launch a platform where copyright owners could host <a href=\"https:\/\/web.archive.org\/web\/20070819022752\/http:\/\/startrek.fanlib.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fan fiction contests<\/a> to boost excitement among fans. But FanLib required submitters &#8212; even those who didn&#8217;t win the contest &#8212; to <a href=\"https:\/\/fanlore.org\/wiki\/FanLib\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">forfeit the rights<\/a> to their work, allowing it to be used for commercial purposes (the platform was <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cbsnews.com\/news\/disney-buying-storytelling-social-net-fanlib-digisynd-in-process\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">sold<\/a> to Disney and shut down two years later). Then, Amazon&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/05\/22\/amazon-debuts-kindle-worlds-where-your-gossip-girl-fan-fiction-can-earn-you-cash\/\">Kindle Worlds<\/a> tried another version of this, authorizing self-published writers to create stories in licensed fictional worlds if they gave up a cut of sales. It didn&#8217;t work either.<\/p>\n<p>Dorian is targeting a different market &#8212; it&#8217;s not about writing &#8220;Harry Potter&#8221; fan fiction, but rather building off of the stories of peer writers on the platform while helping the original authors retain some financial stake in the derivative works they inspire.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Dorian owns the technology, but the creators keep ownership of the IP,&#8221; Palatovska explained. She said that if someone posted an original story on Dorian, and then down the line, the author decided that they want to publish a novel that draws from their Dorian story, that would be allowed.<\/p>\n<p>In select cases, writers can monetize fan fiction based on more popular works &#8212; Dorian <a href=\"https:\/\/www.hollywoodreporter.com\/business\/digital\/lionsgate-dorian-blair-witch-project-1235021881\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">worked with Lionsgate<\/a> to license the \u201cBlair Witch Project&#8221; for a limited-time event last October. But, for example, if someone tried to profit off of &#8220;Supernatural&#8221; fan fiction on Dorian, that wouldn&#8217;t fly, since the IP owner hasn&#8217;t licensed that content to Dorian.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe majority of creators on the platform have been writing fiction and fan fiction for years, and they have never monetized anything,\u201d Palatovska said.<\/p>\n<p>When a fan wants to tell a story based on a game originally published on Dorian, the original author would be able to choose what percentage of royalties to give to fan writers if their derivative stories make money. As long as these derivative creations exist within the Dorian ecosystem, it\u2019s fair game. Still, if a fan writer were to take their derivative works outside of Dorian to monetize them, that\u2019s where they might run into legal issues.<\/p>\n<p>Dorian offers an additional monetization option through livestreaming. Users can livestream themselves playing their own story to generate hype, or they can play through another user\u2019s story (again, the original IP owner could decide the royalty split).<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285766\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285766\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2285766\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png 1170w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=69,150 69w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=139,300 139w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=768,1662 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=314,680 314w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=710,1536 710w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=946,2048 946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Manga-game-creation.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285766\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Dorian<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Though the livestream feature helps creators develop an audience, it\u2019s a bit of a bold move for a relatively new app with a small team. The app, rated for ages 12+, has a predominantly Gen Z audience, and if content moderation tools aren\u2019t in place, something can go wrong very quickly.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019re new, so [content moderation] is definitely something that is on our minds,\u201d Palatovska said. \u201cWe are very happy and lucky to have an extremely well-behaved and collaborative community. It\u2019s nearly 100% female, including the streamers, so we have never had any issues yet. Of course, as we are growing, this might happen, but we\u2019re building some protections.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Currently, hosts can kick people out of their streams if they misbehave, and viewers can report harmful users. Dorian also has its own human moderation team that helps out when possible.<\/p>\n<p>With its new infusion of capital, Dorian plans to grow its team and license IP to host more in-app events like its collaboration with Lionsgate. But as the Ukrainian founder grows her company from San Francisco, she is also coping with the brutal attacks on her home country and trying to help her family, who remain in Ukraine.<\/p>\n<p>Many tech startups are helping <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/how-european-startups-are-aiding-ukrainian-refugees\/\">support Ukrainian refugees<\/a>, but Palatovska\u2019s connection to the conflict is deeply personal. Dorian donated $10,000 to the Ukrainian Army and an additional $10,000 to the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.1kproject.org\/\">1K Project<\/a>, which helps families impacted by the war. It\u2019s estimated that over 3 million Ukrainians refugees have <a href=\"https:\/\/data2.unhcr.org\/en\/situations\/ukraine\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fled their country<\/a> since February 24, and as Dorian creates more roles, the company said it will proactively seek out talent who fled Ukraine or want to relocate when it&#8217;s safe to do so.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"H16lhZ0cy2\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/31\/dorian-seed-funding\/\">Dorian raises $3.25M for its no-code, interactive storytelling platform<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Dorian raises $3.25M for its no-code, interactive storytelling platform&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/31\/dorian-seed-funding\/embed\/#?secret=yWDtYT4WX7#?secret=H16lhZ0cy2\" data-secret=\"H16lhZ0cy2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gcqp2sgnx6\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/26\/inside-realms-of-ruin-ya-novelists-failed-nft-project\/\">Inside the Realms of Ruin<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute;
