without bothering your 4,333 closest friends, who probably follow you because they work in tech, and not because they care that you think that Shake is the most infuriating reality TV villain of all time. Or maybe that&#8217;s just me.<\/p>\n<p>Since last year, Twitter has been <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/court3r\/status\/1410690425963180032\">teasing a feature<\/a> that would allow users to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/01\/twitter-considers-new-features-for-tweeting-only-to-friends-under-different-personas-and-more\/\">customize the audience<\/a> to their tweets, letting them post to only a small subset of their followers. Similar to an Instagram close friends story or Google Plus Circles (<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/08\/looking-back-at-google\/\">RIP<\/a>), Twitter is also calling this product Circle.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Twitter Circle has been leaked by researchers already (h\/t <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/nima_owji?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@nima_owji<\/a>), but we haven&#39;t seen it live yet. I got these pop-ups earlier, but couldn&#39;t click past &quot;got it&quot; on the second screen &#8212; I asked Twitter about it and they said it&#39;s probably a bug! So&#8230; coming soon maybe? <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/uced5XZP21\">pic.twitter.com\/uced5XZP21<\/a><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285585\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>&mdash; amanda silberling (@asilbwrites) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/asilbwrites\/status\/1504148657611980805?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 16, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>This morning, we encountered a pop-up on Twitter prompting us to set up our Twitter Circle to share with a &#8220;smaller crowd&#8221; of up to 150 people. The onboarding screen also indicated that circles can be changed at any time, and people won&#8217;t be notified if you remove them. These were the same screens already <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/nima_owji\/status\/1502367633265598466\">leaked last week<\/a> by app researcher Nima Owji, but when we navigated to the second screen of the onboarding process, we were unable to proceed past the &#8220;got it&#8221; button.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/Twitter?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#Twitter<\/a> is working on the \u201cTwitter Circle\u201d intro page for the web app. <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/mpXyOZhSkD\">pic.twitter.com\/mpXyOZhSkD<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Nima Owji (@nima_owji) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/nima_owji\/status\/1502367633265598466?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 11, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>We asked Twitter about this, and a spokesperson indicated that we likely received the pop-up as a result of a bug, so we couldn&#8217;t actually set up a Twitter Circle since the feature hasn&#8217;t rolled out. But if Twitter is working on this actively enough for an accidental bug to slip through to the real world, it might indicate that we will get our <del>close friends story<\/del> circles soon. Of course, testing a feature, or even rolling it out, doesn&#8217;t mean that it&#8217;s here forever &#8212; remember <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/03\/twitter-fleets-rip\/\">Fleets<\/a>?<\/p>\n<p>Already, through newer features like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/08\/twitter-communities\/\">Communities<\/a> and the option to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/01\/twitter-considers-new-features-for-tweeting-only-to-friends-under-different-personas-and-more\/\">limit replies<\/a> to your tweets, Twitter is giving users more control over who sees their tweets and who can engage with their tweets. You can even paywall your spiciest content through Super Follows. In some ways, part of the joy (and horror) of Twitter is that it&#8217;s like a public square of the internet, and introducing more of these features might make public Twitter feel like LinkedIn, where it would be weird to share your feelings about the &#8220;Love is Blind&#8221; reunion, just to throw out a random example. But users already know (or at least we think they do) that when they post, they&#8217;re making their innermost thoughts public. Historically, tweeters who have wanted to make a more private space to shout into the void have created &#8220;alt&#8221; accounts set to private, which they only share with their inner circle. So, a feature like circles would make it easier to toggle between those two audiences on just one account. Still, the Instagram close friends feature didn&#8217;t necessarily <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/31\/cheugiest-tech-moments-of-2021\/\">end finsta<\/a>.<\/p>\n<div class=\"gmail_default\">&#8220;Twitter is always working on new ways to help people engage in healthy conversations, and we&#8217;re currently exploring ways to let people Tweet to smaller groups. We\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/court3r\/status\/1410690425963180032\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/url?q=https:\/\/twitter.com\/court3r\/status\/1410690425963180032&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1647533298026000&amp;usg=AOvVaw1CidUnwe8AKA8M_0WJOpRB\">previewed<\/a> this concept last year as public feedback helps shape what we build. We don&#8217;t have any further details to share but more to come soon,&#8221; Twitter told TechCrunch.<\/div>\n<div>\n<div dir=\"ltr\" data-smartmail=\"gmail_signature\">\n<div dir=\"ltr\"><\/div>\n<\/div>\n<\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"yKYXyoLiW7\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/01\/twitter-considers-new-features-for-tweeting-only-to-friends-under-different-personas-and-more\/\">Twitter considers new features for tweeting only to friends, under different personas and more<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Twitter considers new features for tweeting only to friends, under different personas and more&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/01\/twitter-considers-new-features-for-tweeting-only-to-friends-under-different-personas-and-more\/embed\/#?secret=pQcZLzbxqC#?secret=yKYXyoLiW7\" data-secret=\"yKYXyoLiW7\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Sometimes you just want to tweet your reactions to the &#8220;Love is Blind&#8221; reunion without bothering your 4,333 closest friends, who probably follow you because they work in tech, and not because they care that you think that Shake is the most infuriating reality TV villain of all time. Or maybe that&#8217;s just me. -companies?tags=115666"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=115666"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=115666"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":61736,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/text-messaging\/","name":"text messaging","slug":"text-messaging","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/61736"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=61736"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=61736"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=61736"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=61736"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":599182,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/twitter\/","name":"Twitter","slug":"twitter","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/599182"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=599182"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=599182"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=599182"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=599182"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2284606,"date":"2022-03-16T07:00:52","date_gmt":"2022-03-16T14:00:52","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2284606"},"modified":"2022-03-16T09:02:37","modified_gmt":"2022-03-16T16:02:37","slug":"linktree-link-in-bio-series-c-valuation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/linktree-link-in-bio-series-c-valuation\/","title":{"rendered":"How much is &#8216;link in bio&#8217; real estate worth? Linktree&#8217;s new valuation says $1.3 billion"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Who would&#8217;ve thought that an entire swath of startups would spring up all because Instagram, TikTok and Twitter only let you link to one website in your bio? Apparently, <a href=\"http:\/\/linktr.ee\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Linktree<\/a> co-founder and CEO Alex Zaccaria did.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We started back in 2016 with a really clear use case to solve this problem for musicians and artists that needed a better way to link out of socials to all their different revenue streams, and we really needed to unify that experience for them to help drive monetization,&#8221; Zaccaria told TechCrunch. &#8220;There was nothing else like [Linktree] that existed. We created this category.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Over the last year and a half, Linktree raised a combined $55.7 million over two funding rounds. Today, the Australia-based company announced a $110 million all equity round led by Index Ventures and Coatue Management, with participation from AirTree Ventures, Insight Partners and Greenoaks. This raise values Linktree at a whopping $1.3 billion. That&#8217;s a lot for what&#8217;s essentially a lightweight mini-website builder.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284606\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>These tools are most useful for influencers or brands. Linktree boasts clients like <a href=\"https:\/\/linktr.ee\/selenagomez\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Selena Gomez<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/linktr.ee\/tiktok\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TikTok<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/linktr.ee\/mlb\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Major League Baseball<\/a>, but even ordinary social media users have found uses for Linktree &#8212; some people use it to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/26\/linktree-raises-10-7m-for-its-lightweight-link-centric-user-profiles\/\">list resources<\/a> to support causes that they care about, or simply direct their friends to their profiles on other platforms.<\/p>\n<p>Like any good idea, other companies tried to spin the idea into something better &#8212; platforms like <a href=\"https:\/\/beacons.ai\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Beacons<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/11\/link-in-bio-monetization-platform-snipfeed-raises-a-5-5m-seed-round\/\">Snipfeed<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/tiktok-charli-damelio-lightricks-facetune\/\">Lightricks<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/23\/streamlabs-launches-a-link-in-bio-website-builder-that-includes-tipping\/\">Streamlabs<\/a> launched link-in-bio builders with an eye on social media creators, but <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Linktree has been able to keep up by introducing its own bells and whistles, like integrations with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/24\/linktree-partners-with-paypal-to-allow-users-globally-to-accept-direct-payments\/\">PayPal<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/11\/linktree-partners-with-shopify-to-allow-users-to-add-storefronts-on-its-platform\/\">Shopify<\/a>. Linktree also recently acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/linktree-announces-acquisition-of-songlinkodesli-and-launches-music-link-feature-301358565.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Songlink\/Odelski<\/a> to create a Music Link feature. With Music Link, artists can paste in the link of their song on any platform, and their Linktree will auto-populate with links to their song on all platforms, rather than individually navigating to each platform to get a link.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re over 24 million users now, with close to 40,000 signups per day,&#8221; Zaccaria said. Just last year, he <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/26\/link-in-bio-company-linktree-raises-45m-series-b-for-its-social-commerce-features\/\">told TechCrunch<\/a> that Linktree had 12 million global users, indicating that, according to the figures provided, Linktree has doubled in size since March 2021.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Linktree is definitely in a hyper-growth phase, and these fundraises really focus on growing the team. We were seven people in March 2020, we&#8217;re now over 230 people globally, and we expect to be hiring another 200 to 300 roles this year between the States and Australia.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"uF1Ulrfekh\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/26\/link-in-bio-company-linktree-raises-45m-series-b-for-its-social-commerce-features\/\">&#8216;Link-in-bio&#8217; company Linktree raises $45M Series B for its social commerce features<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;&#8216;Link-in-bio&#8217; company Linktree raises $45M Series B for its social commerce features&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/26\/link-in-bio-company-linktree-raises-45m-series-b-for-its-social-commerce-features\/embed\/#?secret=kK6U8TOlHy#?secret=uF1Ulrfekh\" data-secret=\"uF1Ulrfekh\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Linktree also just brought on Mike Olson as president &#8212; most recently, he was senior vice president of Growth Initiatives at Twitch. At Linktree, Olson will focus on United States market expansion.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re based in Australia and the majority of our team is here, but most of our users are in the U.S.,&#8221; Zaccaria told TechCrunch. &#8220;We&#8217;re looking to scale that team there a lot.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Linktree offers users four different <a href=\"https:\/\/linktr.ee\/s\/pricing\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">subscription options<\/a>, ranging from free to $21 per month. The paid options offer more customization and expanded creator monetization tools. Right now, Linktree doesn&#8217;t take a cut of transactions (besides standard credit card fees) when users send a creator a tip, buy a product through the Shopify integration or book a request (i.e. creators can offer Cameo-like video shoutouts as a paid digital good on their Linktree). But eventually, Linktree plans to start taking a cut, and that percentage decreases from 10% to 0.5% as your monthly payment increases. So, for a larger creator, shelling out $21 a month to lower Linktree&#8217;s cut from 10% to 0.5% could be financially beneficial. Linktree says that it helped\u00a01.7 million people drive 1.2 billion clicks to commerce-related websites in the last year alone.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;What you&#8217;re seeing on the pricing page right now is to give users a heads up on what that will be, but right now, we&#8217;re not charging at all,&#8221; Zaccaria said. &#8220;We call it a promotional period right now &#8212; we just launched the partnerships [with Shopify, Square and PayPal] over the last year, and we&#8217;re helping creators just drive their revenue and be able to get their foot in the door and start using those products without getting extra fees.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>So, despite now being valued at over $1 billion, Linktree&#8217;s current revenue streams are limited to monthly subscriptions. Linktree declined to share any revenue numbers, including what percentage of its 24 million users are paid subscribers, or whether or not the company is profitable yet.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Everything is hyper-focused on this idea that if we add value to users, if we help them win, perhaps they&#8217;ll pay for adding value to their lives by way of reaching their audience, converting more, getting better results or saving them time,&#8221; Zaccaria said. &#8220;We&#8217;re really focused on helping creatives save time and help them run their business.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Update, 3\/16\/21, 10:50 AM: A previous version of this article called Linktree&#8217;s $110 million fundraise a Series C round; Linktree clarified that this is actually an extension of the company&#8217;s March 2021 Series B round.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"8G0CJCYMAz\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/tiktok-charli-damelio-lightricks-facetune\/\">TikTok star Charli D&#8217;Amelio and family back Facetune maker Lightricks<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;TikTok star Charli D&#8217;Amelio and family back Facetune maker Lightricks&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/tiktok-charli-damelio-lightricks-facetune\/embed\/#?secret=x4mHAwKzIP#?secret=8G0CJCYMAz\" data-secret=\"8G0CJCYMAz\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Who would&#8217;ve thought that an entire swath of startups would spring up all because Instagram, TikTok and Twitter only let you link to one website in your bio? Apparently, Linktree co-founder and CEO Alex Zaccaria did. &#8220;We started back in 2016 with a really clear use case to solve this problem for musicians and artists will add basic parental supervision tools to its VR headset almost three years after launch"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Despite releasing its <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/21\/oculus-quest-and-rift-s-now-shipping\/\">first virtual reality headsets<\/a> in May 2019, Meta is only now <a href=\"https:\/\/about.fb.com\/news\/2022\/03\/vr-parental-supervision-tools-on-quest\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">adding<\/a> parental supervision tools to its Meta Quest VR headset.<\/p>\n<p>After last year&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/28\/facebook-changes-its-corporate-branding-to-meta\/\">rebranding spectacle<\/a>, all eyes are on Meta as it tries to prove that its investments in VR were worth changing its name over. But with attention from <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/biden-social-media-mental-health-state-of-the-union\/\">the highest office in the United States<\/a> on its safety features, Meta is trying to make its platforms safer for kids by rolling out a variety of parental supervision tools.<\/p>\n<p>Sales of the Meta Quest 2 skyrocketed during the 2021 holiday season &#8212; in the two weeks following Christmas Day, estimates show that the Oculus Quest mobile companion app was downloaded around <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/meta-had-a-good-holiday-as-its-oculus-vr-companion-app-gained-2m-downloads-since-christmas\/\">two million times<\/a>. But as Meta&#8217;s headset became more popular, the lack of parental controls became a more <a href=\"https:\/\/lifehacker.com\/how-to-set-up-your-own-parental-controls-on-oculus-ques-1848617852\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">glaring issue<\/a>. The U.K.&#8217;s Information Commissioner&#8217;s Office applied added pressure by suggesting that the headset <a href=\"https:\/\/www.theguardian.com\/technology\/2022\/jan\/09\/uk-data-watchdog-seeks-talks-with-meta-over-child-protection-concerns\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">could breach<\/a>\u00a0its online children&#8217;s safety code.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2285185\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285315\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285315\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2285315\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"614\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg 1238w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg?resize=150,90 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg?resize=300,180 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg?resize=768,460 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg?resize=680,408 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.10.06-AM.jpg?resize=50,30 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285315\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Meta<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Currently, Quest headsets allow users to set up an unlock pattern, like a passcode, to gain access to their device. In April, Meta said it will extend this functionality to apply to specific apps. That way, if a parent doesn&#8217;t want their child playing a certain game on a shared headset, they can set a specific unlock code for that app.<\/p>\n<p>In May, Meta plans to add a feature that will automatically block teens from downloading apps that are deemed inappropriate for their age group by the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.globalratings.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">IARC<\/a> (Quest profiles are connected to Facebook accounts, which is how the platform knows your age). Still, if a young teen is using an account associated with their parent&#8217;s login, this defense may not be effective.<\/p>\n<p>Over the coming months, Meta will continue to build out its suite of parental controls on the Quest. Through the Oculus mobile apps, parents will be able to access a Parent Dashboard, which allows parents to link to their child&#8217;s account.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The company <a href=\"https:\/\/about.fb.com\/news\/2022\/03\/parental-supervision-tools-instagram-vr\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">additionally opened<\/a> a <a href=\"http:\/\/meta.com\/familycenter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Family Center<\/a> to organize its tools and other parental resources.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2285317\" style=\"width: 674px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2285317\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\" wp-image-2285317\" https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.09.56-AM.jpg?resize=768,756 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.09.56-AM.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-16-at-9.09.56-AM.jpg?resize=64,64 64w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 664px) 100vw, 664px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2285317\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Meta<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The process is initiated by the teen, and both the parent and teen have to agree to the experience,&#8221; Meta wrote in <a href=\"https:\/\/about.fb.com\/news\/2022\/03\/vr-parental-supervision-tools-on-quest\/\">a blog post.<\/a><\/p>\n<p>Housing these VR supervision tools in a mobile app is a smart move for parents who may feel more comfortable operating a mobile app than a VR headset. Through this mobile dashboard, parents can manage which apps their child can download according to their rating &#8212; so, for example, a parent could pre-authorize their teen&#8217;s account to download any all-ages apps. If a teen wants to purchase a paid app, the parent can approve or deny the request. The parent can also block the child from accessing certain apps, including the web browser and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.oculus.com\/blog\/oculus-quest-platform-updates-oculus-link-exits-beta-introducing-oculus-move-and-more\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Link<\/a>, which connects Quest headsets to PC VR games. Additionally, parents can view their child&#8217;s screen time, friends list and downloaded apps.<\/p>\n<p>Quest headsets are intended for users age 13 and up, but of course, younger children will inevitably find their way into virtual reality. Even for teens, though, some apps are gated by age, like &#8220;Horizon Worlds&#8221; and &#8220;Horizon Venues,&#8221; two of Meta&#8217;s social VR apps.<\/p>\n<p>Only in the &#8220;Horizon Worlds&#8221; welcome plaza are there any human moderators present, but their job seems more geared toward helping users who might have questions about how to take a selfie in the metaverse.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xlal93q9t4\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/meta-had-a-good-holiday-as-its-oculus-vr-companion-app-gained-2m-downloads-since-christmas\/\">Meta&#8217;s Oculus VR companion app gained ~2M downloads since Christmas<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Meta&#8217;s Oculus VR companion app gained ~2M downloads since Christmas&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/meta-had-a-good-holiday-as-its-oculus-vr-companion-app-gained-2m-downloads-since-christmas\/embed\/#?secret=MwmfhZCWk5#?secret=xlal93q9t4\" data-secret=\"xlal93q9t4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;Horizon Worlds&#8221; has already been exploited for under-developed content moderation systems. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.buzzfeednews.com\/article\/emilybakerwhite\/meta-facebook-horizon-vr-content-rules-test\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">BuzzFeed reported<\/a> that it created a test world filled with content that&#8217;s banned from Facebook and Instagram, like QAnon conspiracies, but Meta&#8217;s content moderation system said that it didn&#8217;t violate guidelines. Some users even <a href=\"https:\/\/www.technologyreview.com\/2021\/12\/16\/1042516\/the-metaverse-has-a-groping-problem\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> being sexually harassed and groped on the platform. Unfortunately, these experiences take place even on text-based web forums, but this kind of harassment can feel especially intense while in an immersive, unfamiliar virtual world. So far, Meta has instituted an <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/meta-to-allow-horizon-worlds-users-to-turn-their-avatars-personal-safety-boundary-off-despite-virtual-world-sexual-assaults\/\">optional personal boundary<\/a> feature in an attempt to curb this behavior.<\/p>\n<p>TechCrunch asked Meta for comment about how it can gate users under the age of 18 from accessing apps like &#8220;Horizon Worlds,&#8221; since <a href=\"https:\/\/slate.com\/transcripts\/eW82bTg3MTBIN2ZVaThoN042U3dmSFNjY2ExT3kxSVN4T21MU0xKMTEybz0=\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">many users<\/a> reported that the platform is already <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/technology\/2022\/02\/07\/facebook-metaverse-horizon-worlds-kids-safety\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">overrun<\/a> with children &#8212; several <a href=\"https:\/\/www.oculus.com\/experiences\/quest\/2532035600194083\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reviews of the app<\/a> in the Quest Store include complaints about being followed around by misbehaving children.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Today marks the first step on a longer journey and we plan to add more options over time,&#8221; a Meta representative told TechCrunch. They pointed to app-specific unlock patterns as a potential solution, but this only keeps children off the 18+ platform if their parent has the knowledge and foresight to do so. &#8220;Our parental supervision tools features will continue to develop and expand over time as we learn more about what parents and teens need from our platform.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Ultimately, parental controls are only effective if parents and teens use them well &#8212; but rolling out these guardrails is the least Meta can do.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"aVeYwRkW5E\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/meta-to-allow-horizon-worlds-users-to-turn-their-avatars-personal-safety-boundary-off-despite-virtual-world-sexual-assaults\/\">Meta to allow Horizon Worlds users to turn their avatar&#8217;s personal safety boundary off<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Meta to allow Horizon Worlds users to turn their avatar&#8217;s personal safety boundary off&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/meta-to-allow-horizon-worlds-users-to-turn-their-avatars-personal-safety-boundary-off-despite-virtual-world-sexual-assaults\/embed\/#?secret=DNnSu4ipq0#?secret=aVeYwRkW5E\" data-secret=\"aVeYwRkW5E\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Sw4XxxatJy\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/biden-social-media-mental-health-state-of-the-union\/\">Biden will address social media&#8217;s mental health impact at State of the Union<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; \/wp\/v2\/tags\/576603748"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576603748"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576603748"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576603748"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576603748"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6521415,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/oculus\/","name":"Oculus","slug":"oculus","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6521415"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6521415"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6521415"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6521415"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6521415"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":30787,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/product-management\/","name":"product management","slug":"product-management","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/30787"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=30787"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=30787"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=30787"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=30787"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":85590,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/quest\/","name":"Quest","slug":"quest","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/85590"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=85590"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=85590"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=85590"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=85590"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2283706,"date":"2022-03-12T09:00:16","date_gmt":"2022-03-12T17:00:16","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2283706"},"modified":"2022-03-14T07:19:10","modified_gmt":"2022-03-14T14:19:10","slug":"david-dobrik-documentary-premieres-sxsw-casey-neistat-reveals-youtube-dangers","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/12\/david-dobrik-documentary-premieres-sxsw-casey-neistat-reveals-youtube-dangers\/","title":{"rendered":"Casey Neistat\u2019s David Dobrik documentary explores what happens when creators cross the line"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">\u201cThere\u2019s three different<\/span> things that make up a vlog,\u201d David Dobrik, then a rising YouTube star, explained to Casey Neistat, a veteran YouTuber and filmmaker. Neistat\u2019s camera pans to show a swimming pool, where a member of Dobrik\u2019s ensemble, the Vlog Squad, balances on a jet ski, attempting to toss a basketball from half-court distance over his shoulder and into a hoop. \u201cIt\u2019s like, interesting things, cool visuals and funny stuff. And this is not funny unless someone gets hurt.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>As Dobrik&#8217;s following grew, his stunts became more elaborate. People got hurt. It wasn\u2019t funny.<\/p>\n<p>When Neistat began filming his first feature-length documentary \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/schedule.sxsw.com\/2022\/films\/2054014\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Under the Influence<\/a>\u201d in 2019, the older, wiser YouTube star wanted to capture the phenomenon of David Dobrik, the then-22-year-old and <a href=\"https:\/\/rewind.youtube\/about\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fifth most-viewed<\/a> creator on the platform. Neistat followed Dobrik as he moved into multimillion-dollar homes, performed for crowds of screaming college kids and bought his friends Teslas as casually as if treating them to lunch at Chipotle (where they could have ordered <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.chipotle.com\/2019-04-03-Chipotle-Offers-Free-Delivery-And-Teams-Up-With-David-Dobrik-To-Celebrate-National-Burrito-Day\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dobrik-branded burritos<\/a>).<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283706\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Now, as \u201cUnder the Influence\u201d premieres at SXSW, Neistat is telling a far different story than the one he set out to document. In fact, he threw out two years of post-production work once his already-controversial muse became a bonafide persona non grata online.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI definitely started the process of making this movie in good faith. I think it was undeniable, David\u2019s phenomenon. That\u2019s not to praise the content he was making itself, but certainly, the phenomenon that was David was something absolutely extraordinary,\u201d Neistat told TechCrunch. \u201cIt was clear that his content, I think to say it generously, was walking a very fine line, even back then.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>At the time, Dobrik was on top of the world, filming prank videos with celebrities like <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=hTMt0wpPfyY\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Kylie Jenner<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=6VF0GEf3S0I\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Justin Bieber<\/a> and transcending the bounds of social media to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=KxZS0gv7J5g\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">make guest appearances<\/a> on \u201cLate Night with Jimmy Fallon.\u201d But his pedestal was built on the sheer luck that he got away with so many dangerous stunts. Eventually, Dobrik went far enough that it toppled over.<\/p>\n<p>Within two years \u2013 as Neistat continued to document \u2013 Dobrik found himself at the center of two serious scandals. In March 2021, Insider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/vlog-squad-durte-dom-rape-allegation-david-dobrik-zeglaitis-video-2021-3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> that a woman in one of his videos claimed to have been sexually assaulted by a Vlog Squad member on the night they filmed a video about group sex.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Dobrik lost sponsorships with brands like Hello Fresh, SeatGeek, EA Sports and DoorDash; he was <a href=\"https:\/\/variety.com\/2021\/digital\/news\/david-dobrik-youtube-demonetized-1234938946\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">demonetized<\/a> on YouTube; and he stepped down from Dispo, the venture-funded social photo-sharing app that he co-founded. Early investors including Spark Capital, Seven Seven Six and Unshackled committed to donate <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/22\/early-investors-in-dispo-to-donate-any-profits-from-the-photo-sharing-app\/\">any potential profits<\/a> from their investment in the app to organizations working with survivors of sexual assault.<\/p>\n<p>But all the while, Dobrik was hiding another secret: The year before, a risky stunt went so wrong that his friend and collaborator Jeff Wittek nearly died.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2283708\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2283708\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2283708\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"David Dobrik documentary film still\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_002_wcolor-1.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2283708\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Casey Neistat<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<h2><strong>&#8220;There was no such thing as a \u2018power dynamic\u2019 to me&#8221;<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Dobrik\u2019s stunts were always dangerous. When Neistat first visited his mansion in 2019, Dobrik greeted him at the door with a flamethrower, which he wielded haphazardly, like a Nerf gun.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">\u201cThere was never a naivety on my part, even in my relationship with David, that everything was perfect,\u201d Neistat told TechCrunch. \u201cPart of my interest in telling this story was to try to reveal how this is done, and how he tried to get away with what he was getting away with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Yet documenting the highs and lows of Dobrik\u2019s at-times dangerous pursuits is arguably its own flavor of sensationalism.<\/p>\n<p>Early in the documentary, when Jonah (whose real name is Nick Antonyan \u2013 he\u2019s called Jonah in the vlogs because he looks like Jonah Hill, and his body type often makes him the butt of hurtful jokes) drives a motorbike over a ramp and into a pool, he punctures a hole in his stomach.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cLet\u2019s get Jonah to the hospital, and David, let\u2019s get this footage into editing,\u201d a Vlog Squad member told Dobrik.<\/p>\n<p>Jonah proved to be OK after his trip to the emergency room, yet this near-miss didn\u2019t appear to be a wakeup call for Dobrik, who continued to pursue the next biggest stunt, regardless of whether it could put his friends \u2013 who also acted as business collaborators \u2013 in danger.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI remember very clearly, one of the first questions I asked David was, \u2018These people that we\u2019ve seen in your videos, are they your friends or your coworkers?\u2019 And his response, that\u2019s included in the movie, is \u2026 he hesitates,\u201d Neistat said. \u201cIt caught me off guard, because I expected him to be almost offended at that question.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Dobrik\u2019s newfound wealth gave him access to flamethrowers, motorcycles, jet skis and heavy machinery for riskier stunts, but unlike Hollywood, where on-set stunts are heavily regulated, Dobrik was not required to hire safety professionals, so he didn\u2019t.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s certainly an understandable suggestion to draw parallels between the content that David made and something like &#8216;Jackass,&#8217; but there\u2019s one extraordinary, bold line between the two, and that line is one of consent,\u201d Neistat told TechCrunch. \u201cSteve-O is a friend of mine, and every member of the \u2018Jackass\u2019 team knows exactly what they\u2019re signing up for. They know what the cost is going to be to them physically. They know what their liability is, they know what their return is, they know what the transaction is. It is consensual, and I think that is the extraordinary difference between the things that you see on YouTube \u2013 especially when you\u2019re looking at sort of an ensemble cast of characters like David\u2019s videos \u2013 and something like \u2018Jackass.\u2019\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Of course, accidents still happen in Hollywood, but on YouTube, there\u2019s no possible way that a platform could regulate what happens during filming, even if it wanted to.<\/p>\n<p>Even though YouTube bans \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/support.google.com\/youtube\/thread\/1063345?hl=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">dangerous or threatening pranks<\/a>,\u201d the guideline is usually only enforced to stop people from participating in potentially deadly viral challenges. When YouTube <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/01\/15\/youtube-will-ramp-up-enforcement-of-its-policies-against-dangerous-challenges-and-pranks\/\">added the rule<\/a> in 2019, the company specifically referenced trends like people <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/news\/to-your-health\/wp\/2018\/01\/13\/teens-are-daring-each-other-to-eat-tide-pods-we-dont-need-to-tell-you-thats-a-bad-idea\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">eating Tide Pods<\/a> or trying to light themselves on <a href=\"https:\/\/www.newsweek.com\/fire-challenge-tiktok-trend-13-year-old-injured-1596392\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fire<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>While Dobrik\u2019s pranks could (and did) cause serious injury, his videos weren\u2019t removed from YouTube.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe don\u2019t allow pranks that make victims believe they\u2019re in serious physical danger \u2013 for example, a home invasion prank or a drive-by shooting prank,\u201d YouTube <a href=\"https:\/\/support.google.com\/youtube\/thread\/1063345?hl=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wrote<\/a> at the time. \u201cWe also don\u2019t allow pranks that cause children to experience severe emotional distress, meaning something so bad that it could leave the child traumatized for life.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Many of YouTube\u2019s biggest stars have followed this same formula \u2013 they start with low-budget pranks, and as their channels pick up steam and bring them riches, there\u2019s no boundary to the potential for their antics. It\u2019s a form of wish-fulfillment for young viewers \u2013 if you and your friends lived in a big mansion with unlimited cash, what mischief would you get up to?<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThis endless pursuit of sensationalism is where I think someone like David lives. The more sensational it was, the crazier the stunts, the more views it had,\u201d Neistat said. \u201cA number of creators on YouTube have pursued a similar trajectory, and it has never ended well.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>YouTube\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/trends\/2021\/us\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">top trending video<\/a> of 2021 featured Jimmy Donaldson (<a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/channel\/UCX6OQ3DkcsbYNE6H8uQQuVA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">MrBeast<\/a>) following a similar <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/03\/mrbeast-squid-game-creator-economy-viral\/?tpcc=tcplustwitter\">pursuit of sensationalism<\/a> \u2013 he <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=9bqk6ZUsKyA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">buried himself alive<\/a> for 50 hours, though Donaldson did hire a medic to keep watch on standby.<\/p>\n<p>Another prominent YouTuber, Logan Paul, faced consequences for prioritizing shock value over his responsibility as a creator with a massive platform. In conversation with TechCrunch, Neistat brought up Paul\u2019s \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/www.nbcnews.com\/pop-culture\/pop-culture-news\/youtuber-logan-paul-sued-over-suicide-forest-video-n1252610\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">suicide forest<\/a>\u201d scandal, in which the YouTuber visited a Japanese forest known to be a common site of suicides and made jokes about a dead body he encountered. YouTube <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bbc.com\/news\/world-asia-42644321\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cut ties<\/a> with Paul, who <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/LoganPaul\/status\/948026294066864128\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said<\/a> his poor judgment was a result of being \u201cmisguided by shock and awe.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Similarly, YouTube <a href=\"https:\/\/variety.com\/2021\/digital\/news\/david-dobrik-youtube-demonetized-1234938946\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">demonetized<\/a> Dobrik\u2019s channels in the aftermath of the sexual assault allegations against a member of his Vlog Squad. Recently, Dobrik <a href=\"https:\/\/www.tubefilter.com\/2022\/01\/03\/david-dobrik-no-youtube-money-three-years\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said on his podcast<\/a> that he still isn\u2019t making money on YouTube. TechCrunch asked YouTube if Dobrik\u2019s channels remain demonetized, but did not receive a response.<\/p>\n<p>On screen, Neistat asked Dobrik, \u201cThere\u2019s something gross about a guy using his social media platform and his influence to attract young women, and then you make a video out of it. Did any of that occur to you as wrong or inappropriate?\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAt that time, there was no such thing as a \u2018power dynamic\u2019 to me,\u201d Dobrik replied in the documentary \u2013 an admission that he never considered how his position as a super-sized social media star could change the way people interacted with him. \u201cI didn\u2019t see that as anything weird. Looking back at it now, it\u2019s really gross.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2283710\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2283710\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2283710\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"David Dobrik documentary film still\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg 960w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/UTI_041_wcolor_1.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2283710\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Casey Neistat<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<h2><strong>&#8220;I should be dead&#8221;<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>A month after the Insider article was published, another bomb dropped: Vlog Squad member Jeff Wittek revealed in his own YouTube <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=PTuJLt6tz1I\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">documentary<\/a> that, the previous year, Dobrik had swung him around on an excavator. The construction equipment requires a license to operate, and Dobrik didn\u2019t have that or any other safety supervision for the stunt.<\/p>\n<p>Dobrik subsequently lost control of the heavy machinery and, as Neistat depicts in a horrifyingly gory scene, Wittek slammed into the side of the crane and broke open the side of his face. Since then, Wittek has had at least nine eye surgeries and cut ties with Dobrik, who continues to pay his medical bills.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI shouldn\u2019t be here anymore,\u201d Wittek told Neistat in the film. \u201cI should be dead.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Neistat told TechCrunch that Dobrik has seen the documentary, but they haven\u2019t spoken about it \u2013 in fact, they haven\u2019t spoken since their final interview, which took place after Insider published sexual assault allegations against Dobrik\u2019s collaborator. TechCrunch asked Dobrik\u2019s team for comment on the film, but did not hear back before publication.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cJeff\u2019s accident had a tremendous impact on how I was conducting interviews, and my professional relationship with David,\u201d Neistat said. \u201cAnd then when Kat\u2019s article came out, that was a dramatic, dramatic shift in how the movie was captured.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt was very heavy, and you can hear in the tone of my voice just how it kind of became a little bit more contentious, and I became more confrontational with him. In that final interview, I think one of the first questions I asked him was, \u2018Do you feel responsible?\u2019\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In a podcast published days before \u201cUnder the Influence\u201d premiered at SXSW, Dobrik expressed <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=gRMQg2dEo_0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">remorse<\/a> for the egregious incidents that the documentary centers around. Yet in the documentary, he doesn\u2019t seem to grasp the implications of his mistakes.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe [Insider article] was written because this place wanted clicks, like, it wasn\u2019t written because the company\u2019s going and looking after the victim and making sure she\u2019s OK,\u201d Dobrik said to Neistat in the documentary.<\/p>\n<p>A few weeks ago, Wittek made a podcast episode called \u201cDear David\u2026\u201d about why he was no longer friends with the figure who propelled him to fame.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI\u2019ll have life-long brain injuries, and I saved him from fucking everything. He could\u2019ve got deported, he could\u2019ve got put in jail for manslaughter, he could\u2019ve got sued for everything,\u201d Wittek said on <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=bz2SNSHes1M&amp;feature=youtu.be\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">his podcast<\/a>. \u201cI took it on the chin, and then to see [the documentary] &#8230; that just made me completely lose all respect for this guy, and lose all hope he could ever turn around and become a better person.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Dobrik\u2019s career has certainly taken a sizable hit, but he continues to post on YouTube, where he still has 18.3 million subscribers. He even has a Discovery show called \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/www.discovery.com\/shows\/discovering-david-dobrik\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Discovering David Dobrik<\/a>,\u201d a docuseries in which he travels the world with his friends. The show was <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Discovery\/status\/1435377343229431809?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1435377343229431809%7Ctwgr%5E%7Ctwcon%5Es1_&amp;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.insider.com%2Fdavid-dobrik-vlog-squad-discovery-travel-show-deal-2021-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced and filmed<\/a> after both of these scandals came to light.<\/p>\n<p>Even in his first interview with Dobrik, Neistat observed that the young star looked haggard and overworked.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s prescient to see it now,\u201d Neistat told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>But it\u2019s not a coincidence that so many top YouTubers like Dobrik, Donaldson and Paul follow this same trajectory: They strive to make each video more engaging than the last, but eventually, there seems to be just two paths. Either you burn out or make a career-altering mistake before you take a beat to slow down.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI think that there\u2019s always a pursuit. It\u2019s relevant for a musician \u2013 how do you keep your music interesting?\u201d Neistat said. \u201cBut what makes individuals like David Dobrik different is that their pursuit is not coming out with the next song or making the next movie. Their pursuit is, how can I be more sensationalist? And that is a very, very, very dangerous pursuit, because the minute you achieve something that was crazier than the last, you then have to go past that.\u201d<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>\u201cThere\u2019s three different things that make up a vlog,\u201d David Dobrik, then a rising YouTube star, explained to Casey Neistat, a veteran YouTuber and filmmaker. Neistat\u2019s camera pans to show a swimming pool, where a member of Dobrik\u2019s ensemble, the Vlog Squad, balances on a jet ski, attempting to toss a basketball from half-court distance is working on a podcasts tab"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As Twitter <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/07\/twitter-spaces-continues-testing-podcast-like-features\/\">continues to develop<\/a> its live audio product Spaces, the platform may soon take things a step further by launching a dedicated podcasts tab on its mobile apps.<\/p>\n<p>According to reverse engineers who search the code of mobile apps to spot features in development, this addition would create a dedicated space on Twitter to house podcasts.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/Twitter?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#Twitter<\/a> is working on Podcasts \ud83d\udc40 <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/CqBm1qHV5H\">pic.twitter.com\/CqBm1qHV5H<\/a><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280070\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>&mdash; Alessandro Paluzzi (@alex193a) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/alex193a\/status\/1499109649961869318?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 2, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>We asked Twitter if users could expect this feature to roll out. A spokesperson said, &#8220;We\u2019re always exploring new ways to help people engage in the conversation on Twitter, but have no further details to share at this time.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Twitter has worked on a number of podcast-like features to expand the capabilities of its live audio Spaces. Like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/08\/clubhouse-record-room-replay\/\">Clubhouse<\/a>, Twitter now allows users to listen to Spaces <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/twitter-now-lets-all-ios-android-and-web-users-listen-to-recorded-spaces\/\">after<\/a> the live recording, helping hosts earn greater engagement from a new audience of asynchronous listeners. When users listen to a recorded Space live, they will see a red recording button. Twitter is also rolling out a feature that allows hosts to view <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/07\/twitter-spaces-continues-testing-podcast-like-features\/\">listening stats<\/a> about their recorded Spaces.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Twitter is working on Podcasts tab <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/64tTd3XPdu\">pic.twitter.com\/64tTd3XPdu<\/a><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&mdash; Jane Manchun Wong (@wongmjane) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/wongmjane\/status\/1499110065147551745?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 2, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>A podcasts tab might function like a home for users to browse recorded Spaces and generate more engagement in this content; Twitter already shows live Spaces in their own tab. The podcast snobs among us might note that there is a difference between a live, recorded conversation and a properly edited, sound-designed <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/fintech-tam-explained-by-dating-apps\/\">podcast<\/a>, but&#8230; we&#8217;ll just have to see what Twitter does with this feature before we have that conversation.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"4qauaYL2tg\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/07\/twitter-spaces-continues-testing-podcast-like-features\/\">Twitter Spaces continues testing podcast-like features<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Twitter Spaces continues testing podcast-like features&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/07\/twitter-spaces-continues-testing-podcast-like-features\/embed\/#?secret=BsCvaII8UU#?secret=4qauaYL2tg\" data-secret=\"4qauaYL2tg\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>As Twitter continues to develop its live audio product Spaces, the platform may soon take things a step further by launching a dedicated podcasts tab on its mobile apps.
